Also relates family history."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/acadian/Sylestine_Rosabel_T733.abs.pdf	"Rosabel Sylestine is of Coushatta Indian heritage and produced pine needle baskets for the Acadian Handicraft Project, a project coordinated through Louisiana State University General Extension to promote and preserve Acadian heritage." Acadian Handicraft Oral History Project	"Ida Duckworth Woods oral history interview, 1995"	"Woods, Ida Duckworth, b. 1911"	1995	"Rabalais, Pamela Pace,; Olivier, Yvonne, -1947"	"Woods discusses her mother's family origins and the harvesting, drying and preparing of palmetto for braiding.  She discusses becoming involved in the Acadian Handicraft Project through her local home demonstration club.  Details include the process of making corn husk dolls and how she found the pattern.  She stopped working for the Acadian Handicraft project when Louise V. Olivier, field representative for the project, died."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/acadian/Woods_Ida_Duckworth_T737.abs.pdf	"Ida Duckworth Woods, born in 1911, worked for the Acadian Handicraft Project making palmetto fans, placemats, and cornshuck dolls during the 1940s - 1960s. She became involved with the Acadian Handicraft project through her local home demonstration agent."	"Woods, Ida Duckworth, b. 1911--Interviews.; Olivier, Louise.; Acadian Handicraft Project.; Progressive farmer.; Cornhusk craft--Louisiana.; Dollmaking--Louisiana--Technique.; Palmetto weaving--Louisiana--Technique.; Weaving--Louisiana--Technique."	1 sound cassette (20 minutes); Transcript (27 leaves)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Ida Duckworth Woods Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.0515, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." Atchafalya Basin Oral History Project	"Aldridge Leroy McMurray Sr. oral history interview, 1979"	"McMurray, Aldridge Leroy"	1979	"Hebert, Sue."	"Interview deals with McMurray's early life and career as a river boat pilot on the Mississippi.  Focus dates of the interview are 1904-1967.  McMurray recalls his father's farming on Chopin Plantation, getting to school, the flood of 1927, and work on government survey boats on the Mississippi.; He describes the government's methods of controlling the River, life on the boats, and getting a pilot's license.  Also mentioned is the debate regarding levees and spillways. The interview was conducted as part of a local history project for the Plaquemine area."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/suehebert/McMurray_AL.pdf	"Master pilot on the Mississippi River and other rivers from the 1920s-1970s. Resident of Bayou Sorrel and Plaquemine, Louisiana, and an employee of Standard Oil, later Esso."	"McMurray, Aldridge Leroy, Sr.--Interviews.; River boats--Louisiana.; Levees--Louisiana.; Pilots and pilotage--Mississippi River."	1 sound cassette (1.5 hour); Transcript (74 p.)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Aldridge Leroy McMurray Sr. Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.0043, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." Atchafalya Basin Oral History Project	"Bill Lindon Rivet oral history interview, 1979"	"Rivet, Bill Lindon, "	1979	"Hebert, Sue."	"Rivet recalls drownings at the Plaquemine locks on the Mississippi River, the sinking of the steamboat Andes, and his work in the mechanical operation of moving boats through the locks.  Rivet describes flood control, the high waters in 1937 or 1938, the work of Gus O'Neil as lock engineer and Mr. Dugal, Jack Roberts, and John W. Abel as lockmasters, repair of leaks, and precautions taken to protect the locks during World War II."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/suehebert/Rivet_Bill.pdf	"River lock worker (1931-1961) and resident of Plaquemine, Louisiana." Baton Rouge History and Culture Oral History Project	"Richard Alden McEwen oral history interview, 1998"	"McEwen, Richard A., "	1998	"Dean, Pamela, -1946"	"McEwen discusses his education; his city planning work in St. Louis, Santa Fe, Richmond, and Baton Rouge; the development of early subdivisions in Baton Rouge; street, drainage, and sewer projects; the Baton Rouge Planning Commission and City Council; urban renewal and the building of the Riverside Centroplex; the influence of petrochemical companies on the development of Baton Rouge; improvement of substandard housing; Mayor Tom Ed McHugh's Horizon Plan for Baton Rouge in the 1980s; and McEwen's role in developing a parking plan for Louisiana State University in 1982."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/brhistory/McEwen_Richard_alltapes.abs.pdf	"Richard Alden McEwen studied landscape architecture at Iowa State University and planned army camp sites during World War II.  He was a city planner in St. Louis, Missouri; Santa Fe, New Mexico; and Richmond, California, before becoming planning director for Baton Rouge, Louisiana in 1953.  He retired in 1980." He is a practicing Catholic, and lives in Cut Off with his wife.  They have four children and five grandchildren." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Augustin J. ""A.J."" LeBlanc, Jr. oral history interview, 2010"	"LeBlanc, A. J. -1936"	2010	"Smith, Courtney,; Hadley, Brooklne,"	"LeBlanc discusses his French Catholic upbringing, and the importance of community, family, and education in his youth.  He talks about his early marriage and career with Humble Oil, and about switching careers into the nascent insurance industry, in which he had financial and professional success.  He discusses the physical and socioeconomic topography of Bayou Lafourche, talking about its changes over the past sixty years, and its current physical reduction and financial inequalities.  He talks about the impact of hurricanes on Bayou Lafourche.  He discusses his family history and his offspring.  He mentions his participation in a community of local French speakers who are trying to preserve the language, and the importance of doing so."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/LeBlanc_Augustin_J_T3939.pdf	"Augustin ""A.J."" LeBlanc, was born July 9, 1936, in Lockport, Louisiana, and is one of three sons of Augustin LeBlanc, Sr.  He grew up speaking French at home, and his house did not have electricity until after World War II.  He was raised, and continues to be, an observant Catholic, and education was always emphasized by his parents.  After high school he married and began working for Humble Oil (now Exxon), but left in 1958 to study insurance marketing at University of Southwest Louisiana.  He set up a State Farm-affiliated practice in Larose, which grew to be very successful.  He and his wife have four children and a number of grandchildren, live in Larose and have a camp in Leeville." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Belonie Scioneaux oral history interview, 2010"	"Scioneaux, Belonie, 1931-2011"	2010	"Philips, Allie,"	"Scioneaux discusses his childhood on a Louisiana plantation and his role in the workforce, as well as his job at the Avondale shipyard. He discusses his first wife and her infidelity, then tells an anecdote about his second wife and her eating habits. Scioneaux enjoys hunting and discusses his various guns, and shooting a rabbit. He explains his limited English, and offers some phrases in French."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Scioneaux_Belonie_T3936.pdf	"Belonie Scioneaux was born in 1931 in Vacherie, Louisiana, the son of Ernest and Martha Scioneaux. His family was employed by a plantation on which they lived, and he began working at a young age. As an adult he worked at Avondale Shipyard for a time before leaving because of health problems. He married at least twice (second wife: Audrey Kraemer Scioneaux), and had several children and stepchildren. Scioneaux, a native French speaker and resident of Chackbay, enjoyed hunting and helping at his daughter's restaurant, Nocko's Deli, until his death in 2011." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Brenda Dardar Robichaux oral history interview, 2010"	"Robichaux, Brenda Dardar, -1958"	2010	"Hayward, David,"	"Robichaux discusses her upbringing in a Houma community just outside of Golden Meadow, Louisiana, and the history of the contentious relationship between the Houma and the white communities of south Louisiana.  The family grew much of its own food, and her father always made sure the family was well fed, even during economically challenging times.  Robichaux discusses the changes in Bayou Lafourche, including the saltwater erosion and the rise in industry in formerly residential communities.  She discusses her grandfather's (Ernest Dardar, a traiteur) role in the community, and recounts the gathering spaces for the family and community, which included the Catholic chapel, her father's boat, and her parents' house."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Robichaux_Brenda_T3946.pdf	"Brenda Dardar Robichaux was born and raised in a Houma Indian community just south of the corporation limits of Golden Meadow, Louisiana.  Her grandfather, Ernest Dardar, was a traiteur, or healer, and her father was a fisherman.  The youngest child in her family, she was among the first Indian students to integrate Bayou Lafourche public schools, and she worked for the parish school district early in her career.  She served as the Principal Chief of the United Houma Nation (1997-2010), and is an outspoken advocate for minority rights.  She has also served on numerous boards (Second Harvest, Inter-Tribal Council of Louisiana, National Indian Education Association, Rockefeller Philanthropy Gulf Coast Ecological Health and Community Renewal Fund Advisory Group, New Orleans Jazz & Heritage) and has won many awards for her service from local and national organizations (Times Picayune, Ms. Foundation, National Coalition on Black Civic Participation, United Houma Nation).  She is married to former state senator Michael Robichaux and has three children: Josh, Jason, and Felicite."	"Robichaux, Brenda Dardar, 1958---Interviews.; Dardar, Ernest.; Catholic Church--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Houma Indians--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Indian healers--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Petroleum industry and trade--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Whites--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish--Relations with Indians.; Golden Meadow (La.)--Social life and customs.; Lafourche Parish (La.)--Social life and customs.; Lafourche, Bayou (La.)--Economic conditions."	1 digital audio file (29 minutes); Abstract (3 leaves); Index (4 leaves)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Brenda Dardar Robichaux Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.2100, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Clyde Orgeron oral history interview, 2010"	"Orgeron, Clyde, -1947"	2010	"Donovan, Erin,; Shelby, Christina,"	"Orgeron discusses his childhood, growing up on a farm in Valentine, Louisiana.  He recounts his early career at the Freeport Sulphur Company, which eventually moved him from Port Sulphur, Louisiana, to a 7/7 schedule on an offshore rig closer to Bayou Lafourche.  He took correspondence courses and advanced in the company; during his time on land he and his wife were busy building a new home and starting a family.  Orgeron discusses how he came to work for the Louisiana Offshore Oil Port [LOOP].  He shares his religious beliefs; as a practicing Catholic he goes to church every Sunday and is involved in religious service groups.  He discusses life on the bayou, both in regards to flooding, how things were when he was a boy, and what has changed.  Orgeron sings the Cajun song ""Allons Danser Colinda"" and discusses his recent trip to Nova Scotia and his connection with the people there."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Orgeron_Clyde_T3933.pdf	"Clyde Orgeron, b. 1947, is a Valentine, Louisiana native, the son of Augustin Fortunate Orgeron and Nola Barrilleaux Orgeron, who were farmers.  After graduating from public high school in 1966, he worked for Freeport Sulphur Company in Port Sulphur, Louisiana, and was then transferred to a rig off of Grand Isle, Louisiana.  He studied electrical engineering through home correspondence, and was transferred to the electrical and instrumentation department; he stayed with Freeport Sulphur fourteen years, until the company closed.  He took a position with the Louisiana Offshore Oil Port.  Orgeron married in 1968; he and his wife had two children.  He is a practicing Catholic.  In his retirement he lives in Cut Off, Louisiana, and Magnolia, Mississippi." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Evelyn Cheramie Kuyrkendall oral history interview, 2010"	"Kuyrkendall, Evelyn Cheramie, 1950?-"	2010	"Delgado, Natalie,"	"Kuyrkendall grew up in Galliano, Louisiana, a small town in Lafourche Parish.  She discusses her childhood on the bayou, which she enjoyed, although she faced a few challenges because of her hearing impairment (e.g., she couldn't hear threats, like snakes, approaching).  She recalls the transition of moving to the Louisiana School for the Deaf in 1961.  Kuyrkendall discusses her professional life: first at a shrimp factory, then at a grocery store, and then her career as a florist, which she discusses at length, including her year working in Las Vegas, getting her professional license, and the floral shops she helped establish.  Kuyrkendall discusses her Catholic faith, and talks about the challenges of deaf people today, especially in regards to professional opportunities.  She also shares her recollections of Hurricane Betsy (1965), which destroyed her family's home."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Kuyrkendall_Evelyn_T3932.pdf	"Evelyn Cheramie Kuyrkendall was born in Galliano, Louisiana, around 1950.  She attended the local public school from age six to eleven, then in 1961 moved to Baton Rouge to attend the Louisiana School for the Deaf, from which she graduated in 1968.  After working as a flower delivery girl in Bayou Lafourche, in 1974 she moved to Las Vegas to work and train.  Kuyrkendall returned to Louisiana in 1976, and in that year passed her Louisiana State Floral License exam.  She opened three flower shops in south Louisiana, including The General Store Flower & Gift Shop in Golden Meadow, Louisiana, before marrying (1985) and moving to Baton Rouge.  She worked for Edrie's Flower Shop.  She continues to do floral designs for special events, and serves as a house mother at the Louisiana School for the Deaf.  Her daughter Jennifer interpreted most of the interview."	"Kuyrkendall, Evelyn Cheramie, 1950?---Interviews.; Catholic Church--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Louisiana School for the Deaf.; Deaf--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Deaf--Education--Louisiana.; Deaf--Employment--Louisiana.; Florists--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Hurricane Betsy, 1965.; Shrimp industry--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Galliano (La.)--Social life and customs.; Lafourche Parish (La.)--Social life and customs."	1 digital audio file (51 minutes); Abstract (4 leaves); Index (6 leaves)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Evelyn Cheramie Kuyrkendall Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.2140, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Garrett ""Hank"" Danos oral history interview, 2010"	"Danos, Garret, 1950?-"	2010	"Eusea, Olivia,; Dixon, Ashley,"	"Danos discusses his childhood in Larose and Cut Off, La., including his grandfather's sugar cane farm and the slightly more populated neighborhood in Cut Off.  Danos recalls transportation options and the physical construction of the community, and how it was changed.  Danos says living in Bayou Lafourche is defined by pride of culture and independence.  He discusses the oil industry's growth, role, and his contributions through Danos and Curole.  He discusses hurricanes, his current approach to them, and the role the floodgates have had on the local community.  He describes his maternal grandfather's house, as well as the house his parents built in Cut Off.  He also recalls food options on the bayou (groceries and restaurants), then and now."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Danos_Garrett_Hank_T3941.pdf	"Hank Danos was born about 1950 in Larose, La., and grew up there and in Cut Off, La.  He has lived in Lafourche Parish for all his life but the years he attended Louisiana State University, where he earned a B.S. in Business Administration (1971).  He is the CEO and President of Danos, which was founded by his father (as Danos and Curole Marine Contractors); Hank joined in 1971.  Danos is a member of the LSU Board of Supervisors and a number of other state and national boards.  He continues to serve as the head of Danos, which he now runs with his sons.  He is a practicing Catholic and served in the National Guard." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Harold Adams and Louise Adams oral history interview, 2010"	"Adams, Harold, 1946?-"	2010	"Smith, Melissa Michi,"	"Harold and Louise Adams discuss their courtship while they were both students at Nicholls State University in Thibodaux, and the earlier years of their marriage while they were both teachers.  Harold discusses his career as an educator, which includes serving as a teacher and principal in Golden Meadow Public Schools and working for a federal education program.  He also discusses education reform and his approach to discipline and dealing with the parents of students.  Harold discusses the sense of community in Golden Meadow and how it has changed, including Cajun culture and the growth of ethnic and religious diversity.  Harold discusses his, and his children's, relationship with Catholicism.  He discusses the growth of auto culture, the oil industry, and chain commercial stores in the area.  Harold and Louise share memories from Hurricanes Juan and Betsy and the current developments in levee construction in the region.  They discuss concepts of home and community, as well as the role of boats and bridges in the bayou."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Adams_Harold_and_Louise_T3951.pdf	"Harold Adams was born around 1946 in Golden Meadow, La., to Andrew Adams and Letucia Johnfroe Adams.  He grew up on Bobs Lane and attended Golden Meadow School and Nicholls State University as a commuter student.  He married his wife, Louise Adams, in 1969; they were both teachers.  Adams taught at Golden Meadow School, returned to Nicholls to get a master's degree in guidance and psychology, then was asked to be assistant principal of Golden Meadow.  A year later he was promoted to principal, a position in which he stayed until he became a supervisor with federal programs, and retired from education after 33 years.  Harold and Louise Adams are practicing Catholics, have two children and a number of grandchildren.; Louise Adams was born in Larose, La., to a family of grocers.  She attended Nicholls State University and was a teacher.  She married Harold Adams in 1969." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Harold Adams and Reynold ""Ray"" Adams oral history interview, 2010"	"Adams, Harold, 1946?-"	2010	"Smith, Melissa Michi,"	"The brothers discuss their family life, including the ages of their siblings, and the role of Catholicism in their childhood.  They discuss the role of neighbors when they were children, and how their Golden Meadow neighborhood has changed.  Harold discusses his motivations to attend college.  They discuss the oil industry and the growth of wealth on the bayou."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Adams_Harold_and_Ray_T3949.pdf	"Harold Adams was born around 1946 in Golden Meadow, La., to Andrew Adams and Letucia Johnfroe Adams.  He grew up on Bobs Lane and attended Golden Meadow School and Nicholls State University as a commuter student.  He married his wife, Louise Adams, in 1969; they were both teachers.  Adams taught at Golden Meadow School, returned to Nicholls to get a master's degree in guidance and psychology, then was asked to be assistant principal of Golden Meadow.  A year later he was promoted to principal, a position in which he stayed until he became a supervisor with federal programs, and retired from education after 33 years.  Harold and Louise Adams are practicing Catholics, have two children and a number of grandchildren.; Reynold ""Ray"" Adams, Harold's bother, was born in Golden Meadow, La., around 1944 to Andrew Adams and Letucia Johnfroe Adams.  He grew up on Bobs Lane, which was home to the Adams and the Collins extended families.  Adams's father was a refrigeration engineer at an ice plant; Adams also worked there for 13 years after high school.  In 1976 he became a Golden Meadow deputy police officer, and was eventually promoted to chief of police, a position from which he retired.  Adams is a practicing Catholic.  He is married to Judy Adams and has children and four grandchildren." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"John B. ""J.B."" Barnes, Jr. oral history interview, 2010"	"Barnes, J. B. 1923?-2012"	2010	"Tannehill, Mary,"	"Barnes discusses his childhood in Clinton and Baton Rouge, La., which involved being raised by his widowed mother and working from a young age.  The family grew their own food and resources were scarce.  As an adult Barnes helped raise a number of children in Lafourche Parish, and he discusses, at length, how Christian tenets have helped guide his life.  He discusses the history and development of Israelite Baptist Church in Lockport, explaining his role as deacon and as a member of the church choir.  Barnes sings two gospel songs.  He discusses his professional career at Valentine Sugar in Lockport, where he climbed to the rank of overseer/manager, which caused some strain as Barnes is African American and many colleagues were white.  After Valentine closed he worked night shifts at a sugar mill in Raceland. He briefly discusses the non-church community and changes in the physical community of Bayou Lafourche.  Barnes's long medical history is also discussed."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Barnes_John_B_T3948.pdf	"John B. ""J.B."" Barnes, Jr. was born in Clinton, La., around 1923 and was raised with a rural lifestyle in Baton Rouge.  His father died when he was still young, so Barnes was raised by his mother and began to work and contribute to the household at an early age.  He moved to Lockport, La., in 1954 for a job at the Valentine Sugar Company, where he worked on their Valite division and eventually became a plantation overseer, managing the labor force of hundreds, both black and white.  After Valentine's closure in 1979 [1980], Barnes also worked as a water attendant at a sugar house in Raceland.  He was a member of St. John Baptist Church in Clinton and Israelite Baptist Church in Lockport; he served as a church deacon and member of the choir at Israelite Baptist.  Barnes, son of John Barnes, Sr. and Anna Thomas Barnes, was one of many children, and was married to Sally Barnes; the couple had five children and he mentored many more.  He passed away in 2012 and is survived by three sons, one daughter, many grandchildren and great-grandchildren."	"Barnes, J. Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"John Doucet oral history interview, 2010"	"Doucet, John P. "	2010	"Branton, Ryan,"	"Doucet discusses his childhood growing up in Golden Meadow, how he interacted with his father, who was often gone because of his work on the oil rigs, and losing his father at age twelve.  Doucet acknowledges how the community rallied to support him and his brother, including mentors at school and in the extended family, but his family was a close-knit one, and they rarely spent time with the larger community.  Growing up Doucet spent a good deal of time with his grandparents, who spoke Cajun French, and he internalized their language such that he could reproduce many of their characteristics in plays he wrote as an adult.  He also discusses the role and history of French in his family and on the bayou.  The Doucets were very involved in the church, and Doucet served as an altar boy.  Science was important from an early age.  After making a perfect score in a third-grade science exam, Doucet's father, and later teachers, encouraged him to pursue a career in science, which led him to many science fairs and eventually, a doctorate in molecular biology at LSU Medical Center in New Orleans.  He recalls his first memories are of the 1965 Hurricane Betsy, which nearly flooded their house.  His post-doctoral genetic research of Usher's syndrome, which disproportionally affects Acadians, led to the discovery of the genetic mutation responsible, and brought him back to Acadian culture.  He discusses how he got the job at Nicholls and how, since arriving he has continued to conduct genetic research with Acadians and with other subjects of South Louisiana interest, including local animals like love bugs and crawfish.  Doucet discusses the role of religion in his life, with particular emphasis on its intersection with science, and the importance and definition of ""home"" in his life."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Doucet_John_T3945.pdf	"John Doucet was born in 1962 in Golden Meadow, La., the son of Herman Joseph Doucet, an oil field worker, and Dora Rebstock Doucet, a homemaker; he is one of five children.  In his youth he spent a significant amount of time with his French-speaking grandparents, and a good deal of time with his family, but was rather isolated from the larger community.  His father passed away when Doucet was twelve, but before his death encouraged Doucet to study science.  Mentorship in middle school and high school, along with a local, regional, and national recognition, laid the groundwork for Doucet's scientific career.  As a first-generation college student, Doucet studied chemistry at Nicholls State University.  After completing his doctoral studies in biochemistry and molecular biology at Louisiana State University Medical Center in New Orleans, he received a National Institute of Health fellowship to study genetics, also at LSUMC.  His team conducted research on Usher's syndrome, which disproportionately affects people of Acadian descent.  His team identified the genetic mutation that causes Usher's, and his research has continued to focus on people of Acadian descent.  Doucet joined the biology department of Nicholls State in 1999.  He has served as the head of the Biology Department (three years) and honors program (nine years), and in 2012 was selected to serve as Dean of the College of Arts and Sciences.  Doucet became Louisiana's first certified public health geneticist in 2010, and the first to serve on the national Education Board of the American Society of Human Genetics.  He has written over a dozen plays about Louisiana's Cajun culture, and a number of history texts about Bayou Lafourche.  A practicing Catholic, Doucet served as an altar boy; as an adult he continues to have a strong faith in God, which he believes can coexist with his scientific research.  He and his wife, also a Bayou Lafourche native, have two children."	"Doucet, John P.--Interviews.; Catholic Church--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Nicholls State University--Faculty.; Cajun French dialect--Louisiana--Lafourche Parish.; Cajuns--Health and hygiene--Louisiana.; Cajuns--Louisiana--Social life and customs.; Catholic scientists--Louisiana.; Dramatists, American--Louisiana.; Geneticists--Louisiana.; Grandparent and child--Louisiana.; Hurricane Betsy, 1965.; Religion and science--Louisiana.; Usher's syndrome--Research--Louisiana.; Golden Meadow (La.)--Social life and customs.; Lafourche Parish (La.)--Social life and customs." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"John William Barker, Aline Barker and Dee Dee Gaubert oral history interview, 2010"	"Barker, J. W. 1923-2012"	2010	"Barker, Aline Herbert,; Gaubert, Dee Dee,; Drummond, Karrah,"	"Barker recounts his childhood in Lockport, La., which included working and playing with other kids at the Clotilda Plantation.  Barker discusses the sugarcane business, then and now, throughout the interview.  He briefly discusses his education, which included an agricultural engineering degree from Louisiana State University, and his time in the armed forces during World War II at Camp Claiborne, Guadalcanal, and Japan.  He discusses his concept of home and the role of Catholicism in his life.  He and his wife (Aline) and niece (Dee Dee Gaubert) discuss the changes in Bayou Lafourche's commerce with the advent of the oil industry and topography due to erosion.  Aline discusses her family's background and the role of French in her life.  They discuss Valentine Sugar, both the processing of sugarcane and the development of paper products."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Barker_John_et_al._T3937.pdf	"John ""Johnny"" William Barker was born in New Orleans in 1923, and was one of seven children to Frank and Florence Barker.  He spent his first years in a house on Carrollton Avenue, across the street from the Notre Dame Seminary.  His father, a sugar trader, moved the family to the Clotilda Plantation, outside Lockport, La.  Barker attended St. Stanislaus High School and Louisiana State University, where he studied agricultural engineering, and served in the U.S. Army during World War II, serving in the Pacific Theater.  He married Aline Herbert of Larose and the couple had six children and numerous grandchildren.  He is a fourth-generation sugarcane farmer and his professional career included work with Valentine Sugars (where Aline also worked), Bollinger Shipyards, and A.E. Staley.  Barker lived at Clotilda Plantation until his death in 2012."	"Barker, J. Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Larry Williams oral history interview, 2010"	"Williams, Larry, -1947"	2010	"Duplechain, Kayla,; Cosse, Andrew,"	"Williams discusses his childhood in Golden Meadow, both the activities he participated in and also his moral upbringing, which was influenced by his parents and the Catholic Church. He discusses his experience with French at home and at school, and the importance of family. He recalls flooding in Golden Meadow, and mentions (briefly) his time at Nicholls State and serving in the U.S. Army during Vietnam. He explains that he got his job because of a workplace accident which killed his father. He discusses his daughters' education and how the family still socializes around sporting events."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Williams_Larry_T3931.pdf	"Larry Williams was born in 1947 and raised in Golden Meadow, Louisiana, where he spoke both Cajun French with his grandparents and English. He attended Nicholls State University for two semesters and then served the U.S. Army in the Vietnam War, 1966-1968. In that year he married his high school sweetheart and was briefly stationed at Fort Lee, Virginia. He worked at Texaco for his entire career; he secured the job after his father, also a Texaco employee, was killed on a rig explosion. Williams, a practicing Catholic, is still married, but now retired. He has three grown daughters." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Loyman P. Melancon oral history interview, 2010"	"Melancon, Loyman P., -1934"	2010	"Ford, Bruce,"	"Loyman Melancon discusses his childhood as the youngest of five in rural Cut Off, Louisiana, in the 1930s and 1940s, including learning to swim, playing sports, childhood games, trapping with his father, and spending time with his widowed grandmother.  After high school he married and worked in the oil fields, where he advanced through a number of roles, until his father-in-law asked him to join his oyster business.  Melancon speaks at length about oystering, including salinity requirements, leasing and maintenance of oyster beds, dredging fresh oysters, steam plants, canning, predators, and the impact of the 2010 oil spill.  He also discusses the role of French in his upbringing and his current efforts to preserve the language."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Melancon_Loyman_T3938.pdf	"Loyman Melancon was born and raised in Cut Off, Louisiana, the youngest of five siblings.  He grew up in a rural environment, relied on the bayou for transportation, and played sports at Cut Off High School (including on the 1953 six-man football team, which won the state championship).  He married Mamie Eymard after secondary school; the couple had five children.  Melancon worked in the oil industry until his father-in-law asked him to join his oystering business, which included a fleet of four ships.  Melancon joined, and eventually took over, the business, from which he retired in 1985.  In his retirement he travels and participates in groups to preserve Cajun French." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Ophelia Lefort oral history interview, 2010"	"Lefort, Ophelia, "	2010	"Cwieka, Blake,"	"Lefort discusses her childhood on the bayou, including attending a two-room schoolhouse, attending church, trapping with her father, and working at a shrimp shed during World War II.  She recalls meeting her husband in a local movie theater, and discusses her family's genealogical roots.  She tells how she acquired her current residence, which is a converted boarding house for Bayou Lafourche educators, and discusses the motivations and practices she uses in her painting."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Lefort_Ophelia_T3944.pdf	"Ophelia Lefort was born in the late 1920s in Galliano, Louisiana, and raised in the 1930s.  She attended Cut Off High School in the 1940s, and worked at a shrimp shed.  Her first boyfriend was Pershing Lefort (circa 1924-2003), whom she met at the Galliano movie theater; they were engaged before World War II, and married after the war.  The Leforts moved to Lafayette for her husband's education, then returned to Bayou Lafourche, where they raised four children and he worked in the oil industry.  After the youngest of their children was in school, Lefort became a middle school secretary, and began painting in 1985.  Lefort is an accomplished amateur painter, depicting scenes of bayou life on unusual surfaces (oyster shells, cypress shingles, etc.).  She and her late husband bought and preserved a former teacher boarding house in Larose, Louisiana, where she still resides." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Richard Thomas Gibbens Robichaux oral history interview, 2010"	"Robichaux, Richard Thomas Gibbens, -1930"	2010	"Foltz, Kristin,"	"Robichaux discusses his childhood in Thibodaux, including his semi-rural home life (animals in the backyard), places to eat in Thibodaux (including a discussion of home cooking), and the group of boys he termed the ""Hinkety-dinkety Club."" He discusses his musical and parochial education, and how it led to his career as a chaplain's assistant in the Air Force (stationed in Okinawa, Japan), and eventually to playing organ at St. Joseph Co-Cathedral in Thibodaux. Robichaux reflects on Thibodaux's early days (even before he was born, ca. 1900 through the 1940s), and how the damming of Bayou Lafourche at Donaldsonville (1904) has changed the culture of the bayou. Robichaux briefly discusses the sugarcane industry (the family was involved), and how World War II, technology, and television changed the culture of Thibodaux from ""the simple life."" He discusses the construction, growth, and restoration of St. Joseph Co-Cathedral, and also enumerates the events (Masses, weddings, funerals) at which he has played the organ."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Robichaux_Gibbens_T3940.pdf	"R. Gibbens Robichaux was born in 1930 in Thibodaux, Louisiana, son of Alfred G. Robichaux, Sr. and Sara Day Gibbens Robichaux. He had one brother, Alfred G. Robichaux, Jr. (ca. 1928-2012) and was raised in Thibodaux, growing up in a house across the street from his grandparents (Eugene Godfrey Robichaux and Brigeitte Emma Thibodaux Robichaux) and a few blocks from Bayou Lafourche. He attended parochial school; first Mt. Carmel Convent Academy (now the Carmel Inn), and then Brothers of the Sacred Heart School, from which he graduated at sixteen. He met his future wife, Joann, as a teenager. He attended Spring Hill College in Mobile, Alabama (his father is also an alumnus); both he and his dad played piano and had bands in college. Robichaux enlisted in the US Air Force and was stationed for twenty-five months in Okinawa, Japan, where he was a chaplain's assistant and learned to play the organ. He returned to the States, married his wife, and was stationed in Marietta, Georgia. After he returned to Thibodaux he taught briefly (seventh grade), then worked for the welfare office, before becoming the organist of St. Joseph Co-Cathedral in Thibodaux, where he worked for twenty years. He is still involved in the church and music communities in his retirement. He has written a number of children's books, wrote a regular column for the Thibodaux Chamber of Commerce newsletter, and has released three CDs of music." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Ted Savoie oral history interview, 2010"	"Savoie, Ted, -1943"	2010	"Jenkins, Chaffie,; Breaux, Amber,"	"Savoie discusses his grandfather's influence on his early years.  He explains the importance of the Catholic Church in his daily life, growing up, and for his children and their families.  He talks about the role of music and dance halls in his youth, and how he helped to bring musicians to the bayou.  Savoie discusses the importance of volunteering in the community, including his own role in the development of the Oyster Festival.  Savoie discusses the various homes he has lived in, and the changing demographics of Bayou Lafourche, in terms of religion and race."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Savoie_Ted_T3935.pdf	"Ted Savoie was born in 1943 in Galliano, Louisiana, to a family with Acadian heritage (descendants of Fran{cedil}cois Savoie).  He spent his childhood living with his immediate family and maternal grandfather, who was in the oyster business and a community leader.  Savoie's father was originally a farmer from Larose, but entered the oyster business and then the tugboat business, which Savoie eventually took over.  Savoie is active in church and civic activities, and the father of four children and many grandchildren." Bayou Lafourche Oral History Project	"Velton P. Guidry oral history interview, 2010"	"Guidry, Velton P., 1930-2011"	2010	"Lambert, Joshua; Jovicic, Stefan,"	"Guidry discusses his family's genealogy and his interest in Cajun genealogy and historical research in general.  He tells about his education to the seventh grade, which included corporal punishment, and his Catholic upbringing.  His mother worked in a shrimp factory and his father was a fisherman.  His large family was somewhat isolated from the poverty of the depression because they grew so much of their own food and his mother was very resourceful.  Guidry discusses shrimping as a teenager, trapping, and oystering.  He recounts childhood games and beginning to fish at 13.  He recalls a childhood vacation to Barataria Bay, which included harvesting bigorneaux (saltwater snails), a visit to Fort Livingston, and encountering an alligator.  He recalls working on the water during World War II and seeing submarines and other wartime activity.  Guidry also discusses the role of the church in the community (history and physical construction) and in his current life."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/bayoulafourche/Guidry_Velton_T3942.pdf	"Velton Guidry was born in 1930 and lived in Galliano, Louisiana.  He was one of seven children of Gracien and Augusta Choest Guidry.  Velton Guidry was married to Gertrude ""Gertie"" Kiger Guidry, and had two sons, Lenard and Jeffrey.  He served in the U.S. Army, was a fisherman since he was 13, and was an amateur genealogist later in life, focusing on local Cajun culture.  He was a parishioner at St. Joseph Catholic Church in Galliano and died on May 27, 2011." British Voices from South Asia Oral History Project	"Sir Alec Ogilvie oral history interview, 1978"	"Ogilvie, Alec, b. 1913"	1978	"De Caro, F.A., -1943; Jordan, R. A.,"		http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/britishvoices/T853.ind.pdf; http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/britishvoices/T854.ind.pdf	"Sir Alec Ogilvie was born in England, but went to India when he was three months old, where his father was assigned in the British Army's Foreign Political Department.  Educated in England, Ogilvie retruned to India in 1935 where he joined a British company in Calcutta.  He lived in Calcutta until 1965, except during World War II, when he served in the Indian Army from August 1940 to February 1946.  Ogilvie was a Japanese prisoner of war.  Though he began his career in the government, he spent most of his career in private business.  This arrangement resulted from his father's prediction that British political authority would diminish over the next several decades.  He lived in India a total of 36 years and reutned to England at the age of 51." British Voices from South Asia Oral History Project	"Brigadier Frank McCallum, Mrs. Sybilla McCallum, Benjamin and Lady Bromhead oral history interview, 1978"	"McCallum, F. 1900-1983"	1978	"De Caro, F.A., -1943; Jordan, R. A.,"		http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/britishvoices/T879.ind.pdf; http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/britishvoices/T880.ind.pdf	"Brigadier Frank McCallum served in the Indian Army, being commissioned in 1919.  During his career he served as commanding officer of the 10th, 60th, and 24th Indian Brigades; Brigadier General Staff Northern Command; and Director of Staff duties in Pakistan.  Sybilla McCallum (n{acute}ee Barrow) was the daughter of General Sir George de Symons Barrow and Sybilla Way.; Lieutenant-Colonel Sir Benjamin Denis Gonville Bromhead was the son of Major Edward Gonville Bromhead and Emily May Hosking.  He married Nancy Mary Lough, daughter of Thomas Seon Lough, on 6 August 1938.  He fought in the Iraq Campaign in 1920 and in the Waziristan Campaign between 1922 and 1924, where he was wounded.  He fought in the North-West Frontier in 1930, where he was mentioned in despatches.  He gained the rank of Lieutenant-Colonel in the service of the Frontier Force Regiment, Indian Army.  He succeeded to the title of 5th Baronet Bromhead, of Thurlby Hall, co. Lincoln on 31 July 1935.  He fought in the Waziristan Campaign in 1937, where he was mentioned in despatches.  He was Commandant of the Zhob Militia, Baluchistan between 1940 and 1943.  He was invested as a Officer, Order of the British Empire (O.B.E.) in 1943.  He was Political Agent for North Waziristan between February 1945 and April 1947."	"McCallum, F.--(Frank), 1900-1983--Interviews.; McCallum, Sybilla Barrow--Interviews.; Bromhead, Benjamin Denis Gonville, 1900-1981--Interviews.; Bromhead, Nancy Mary Lough, d. 2005--Interviews.; India.--Army--Military life.; British--India--Social life and customs--20th century.; Women--India--Social life and customs--20th century.; Afghan Wars--Personal narratives, British.; India--Economic conditions--1918-1947.; India--Politics and government--1919-1947.; India--Social conditions--20th century." British Voices from South Asia Oral History Project	"Right Reverend Lesslie Newbigin oral history interview, 1978"	"Newbigin, Lesslie, "	1978	"De Caro, F.A., -1943; Jordan, R. A.,"		http://karachi.s-asian.cam.ac.uk/archive/audio/newbigin.html; http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/britishvoices/T884.ind.pdf; http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/britishvoices/T883.ind.pdf	"James Edward Lesslie Newbigin attended Queens College, Cambridge, and was ordained by the Presbytery of Edinburgh to work as a Church of Scotland missionary in Madras, India.  He was Bishop of Madura (Madurai) and Ramnad (Ramanathapuram), Church of South India, between 1947 and 1959.  In 1959 he became the General Secretary of the International Missionary Council and oversaw its integration with the World Council of Churches, to which he became Associate General Secretary.  He remained in Geneva until 1965, when he returned to India as Bishop of Madras, where he remained until his retirement in 1974." Brusly Centennial Oral History Project	"Evanna Jackson-Hodges oral history interview, 1996"	"Jackson-Hodges, Evanna, -1948"	1996	"Bourgeois, Joanne"	"Jackson-Hodges discusses her family, growing up in Brusly, and attending segregated schools in Brusly and Cohn High School in Port Allen.  She primarily discusses attending Brusly High School in 1966, including her academic work and reception by white students, teachers, and policemen.  Jackson-Hodges also describes her attendance at Southern University and teaching in a middle school for the Stockton Unified School District."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/brusly/Jackson-Hodges_Evanna_T1075.abs.pdf	"Evanna Jackson-Hodges was born in Brusly, La., in 1948 to Evanna and Ferman Jackson.  After attending segregated schools through the eleventh grade, Jackson-Hodges enrolled in the integrated Brusly Public School System.  She was the only African American to attend Brusly High School in 1966.  Jackson-Hodges graduted from Southern University in 1970.  She moved to California and taught in the Stockton Unified School District for over 27 years.  She later received a M.S. degree in educational administration."	"Jackson-Hodges, Evanna, 1948---Interviews.; Cohn High School (Port Allen, La.); Brusly High School (Brusly, La.); African Americans--Education--Louisiana--West Baton Rouge Parish.; Public schools--Louisiana--West Baton Rouge Parish.; Segregation in education--Louisiana--West Baton Rouge Parish.; School integration--Louisiana--West Baton Rouge Parish.; Brusly (La.)--History--20th century.; West Baton Rouge Parish (La.)--History--20th century."	1 sound cassette (1 hour); Transcript (55 leaves)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Evanna Jackson-Hodges Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.0741, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." Parker oral history interview, 2003"	"Parker, Dolores D., -1937"	2003	"Parker, Raymond, -1958; Mwendo, Nilima,"	"Parker describes her childhood in various cities in Louisiana, attending her segregated African-American high school in New Orleans in the 1950s, her positions at various schools in New Orleans in the 1960s through 1991, raising four children on her own after she divorced her husband, the Lower Ninth Ward neighborhood before and after Hurricane Betsy, her family's experiences during the hurricane, and their rebuilding process."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/hurricanebetsy/Parker_Dolores_T3342.abs.pdf	"Dolores D. Parker was born in Bayou Goula, La.  The daughter of a minister, she grew up moving around the state.  She graduated from Clark High School in New Orleans then earned a B.A. degree in elementary education from Dillard.  She taught in New Orleans public schools for 32 years and taught reading in an adult education program.  She is the mother of four children: Raymond, Raynelle, Raynette, and Raynard.  Raymond, who also contributes to this interview, is her oldest child." Hurricane Betsy Survivors Oral History Project	"Ida Belle Joshua oral history interview, 2003"	"Joshua, Ida Belle, -1927"	2003	"Mwendo, Nilima,"	"Ida Belle Joshua tells of arriving in the Ninth Ward neighborhood in 1949 and watching it develop as a community.  She described the community as African Americans working in civil service positions with dreams and hopes for the future.  Joshua provides details of Hurricane Betsy's devastation, rescue efforts, federal assistance, and community activism.  She gives her opinion on what should have been done differently following Hurricane Betsy and discusses the recent deterioration of the community because of the lack of activism and community effort."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/hurricanebetsy/Joshua_IdaBelle_T3336.abs.pdf	"Ida Belle Joshua is a native of New Orleans, La., and survivor of Hurricane Betsy.  She moved to the Ninth Ward in 1949 with her husband, Isaac Joshua Sr.  They have three children.  Before Hurricane Betsy, she worked as a hair dresser.  After the storm, she attended the University of New Orleans, Atlanta University (now Clark Atlanta University), and Tulane University and worked as a teacher's aide, social worker, and adjunct professor at Xavier University.  She is a former president of the Lower Ninth Ward Neighborhood Council and Area Beautification Committee and has been an advocate for improvement of the Ninth Ward community.  After Hurricane Katrina in 2005, she temporarily relocated to Lafayette, La.  She intended to return to her home and had begun having it repaired before it was demolished.  She and several other residents sued the city of New Orleans and achieved their goal of preventing the city from demolishing homes without proper notification and hearings for homeowners." Louisiana Civil Rights Movement Oral History Project	"Johnnie Jones, Sr. oral history interview, 1993-1995."	"Jones, Johnnie, -1919"	1993-1995.	"Hebert, Mary J.,"	"Jones gives a detailed account of his life, beginning with his childhood in West Feliciana Parish, La., through his high school, college, and law school education.  He describes his army service in World War II, his position as the first African-American warrant officer, and his involvement the D-Day invasion.  Jones shares recollections of racism, segregation, sit-ins, and protests in Baton Rouge and other Louisiana cities.  He describes in detail his work as a civil rights attorney, including his relationships with Louisiana civil rights leaders, the NAACP, and CORE; his participation in numerous civil rights cases; student activism at Southern University; the Baton Rouge Bus Boycott; his involvement with the NAACP; local and national figures in the civil rights movement; prominent court cases aimed at ending segregation; the lawyers and judges involved in those cases; and the wider civil rights movement in Louisiana."	http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special/williams/abstracts/civilrights/Jones_Johnnie_4700.0321.pdf	"Johnnie Jones, Sr. was born in Laurel Hill, La., in 1919.  After completing sixth grade, he worked for Ransom Lumber Company in Woodville, Miss., where he lived with his boss, Mr. Hergen, and tutored Hergen's son, Buddy.  Jones later was sent to live with his uncle in Scotlandville, La., to begin his high school education at Southern University Demonstration School.  He went on to Southern University for a year and a half until he was drafted into the U.S. Army to serve in World War II.  He was one of the first African-American warrant officers and he took part in the D-Day invasion, landing in the third wave at Omaha Beach.  After the war, Jones returned to Southern University to finish his bachelor's degree in psychology.  After graduating, he married Sebell Chase and worked for two years at the post office.  He then went on to Southern University Law School and earned his law degree in 1953.  Jones' legal career included several landmark civil rights cases."	"Jones, Johnnie, 1919---Interviews.; Tureaud, Alexander Pierre, 1899-1972.; Jemison, T. J.--(Theodore Judson); Cox, B. Elton--(Benjamin Elton), 1931-2011.; Southern University and A & M College.--Demonstration High School.; Southern University and A & M College--Students.; National Association for the Advancement of Colored People.; Congress of Racial Equality.; Actions and defenses--Louisiana--Cases.; African American children--Education--Louisiana.; African American civil rights workers--Louisiana.; African American soldiers.; African Americans--Civil rights--Louisiana.; African Americans--Segregation--Louisiana.; Baton Rouge Bus Boycott, Baton Rouge, La., 1953.; Civil rights movements--Louisiana.; School integration--Louisiana.; Segregation in transportation--Louisiana.; World War, 1939-1945--Participation, African American.; World War, 1939-1945--Campaigns--France--Normandy.; Louisiana--Race relations.; Laurel Hill (La.)" Louisiana Cooperative Extension Oral History Project	"Billy Cochran oral history interview, 2014"	"Cochran, Billy J., "	2014	"Winnie, Wyatt, -1975"	"Cochran begins the interview by discussing his parents' cotton farm. He also talks about life in a rural school and moving to the city of Columbia where he had his first job as a paperboy for the New Orleans Item. The interview then moves into a discussion about his education at Mississippi State, Texas A&M, and Oklahoma State Universities. He documents his time as an LSU professor, an international consultant in the field of agriculture, and his time as a solid waste specialist for the Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/historycoopexten/Cochran_Bill_T4318.abs.pdf	"Billy J. Cochran was born on December 10, 1933, in Darbun, Mississippi. He is the son of Arville Alexander Cochran and Gertrude Lewis. He attended rural Mississippi schools during his youth. In 1958 he graduated with a B.S. degree in agricultural engineering from Mississippi State University. Upon graduation, he served for a short time in the United States Army, and then returned to school at Texas A&M University. In 1962 he graduated with a master's degree in agricultural engineering. In 1964 he joined the faculty at Louisiana State University where he taught in the Agricultural Engineering Department. During the early seventies, he took a sabbatical from LSU and earned a Ph.D. in agricultural engineering from Oklahoma State University. After retiring from LSU in 1983, he worked abroad with the International Rice Research Institute and the Food and Agriculture Organization in Thailand. From 1992 to 1996 he worked for the Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service as a solid waste specialist. He lives in Baton Rouge, La., with his wife, Jintana." Louisiana Cooperative Extension Oral History Project	"Dr. Paul Coreil oral history interview, 2014"	"Coreil, Paul D. "	2014	"Caminita, Cristina M.,"	"Coreil begins the interview by discussing his parents, his early farm life, and working on a farm as a teenager. He details his job as a student worker studying nutria and how that led him to a job with extension services. He describes moving to Cameron Parish, establishing a sea-grant extension program, and the challenges he faced while on the job. These include the Endangered Species Act of the 1970s, a time when shrimpers blockaded a federal ship channel, installing new phone lines in the parish extension office, and how the first computers impacted extension. He also details how farmers now utilize information on the Internet vs. getting it from county agents, the devastation of Hurricanes Katrina and Rita, and how Louisiana Cooperative Extension played a vital role in helping to recover from the storms. He describes what it takes to be successful in extension services and discusses the future of the extension model."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/historycoopexten/Coreil_Paul_T4317.abs.pdf	"Paul Dean Coreil was born on September 9, 1955, in Ville Platte, Louisiana. He is the son of Armand Bertrand Coreil and Juanita Smith. He grew up in Ville Platte, where he attended high school at Sacred Heart Catholic School. In 1976 he graduated with a B.S. in zoology from the University of Southwestern Louisiana. He later attended Louisiana State University where he received a master's degree in wildlife management in 1984 and a Ph.D. in vocational education in 1995. Coreil was involved in the Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service for most of his career. In 1978 he was hired as an assistant area agent for wildlife and fisheries. He also served as Parish Chairman of Cameron Parish LCES, associate specialist of wetland and coastal resources in the state LCES office, and as assistant director of the Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service. In 2001 he was appointed Vice Chancellor and Director of Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service. He retired from LCES in September 2013 and served for a short time as the interim chancellor of LSU-Alexandria."	"Coreil, Paul D.--Interviews.; Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service.; Agricultural extension work--Louisiana.; Agricultural extension work--Louisiana--Cameron Parish.; Cotton farmers--Louisiana--Evangeline Parish.; Coypu--Research--Louisiana.; Hurricane Katrina, 2005.; Hurricane Rita, 2005.; Ville Platte (La.)--Social life and customs--20th century." Louisiana Cooperative Extension Oral History Project	"Gina E. Eubanks oral history interview, 2014"	"Eubanks, Gina Elaine, -1956"	2014	"Winnie, Wyatt, -1975"	"Eubanks discusses her early life in Clinton, East Feliciana Parish, Louisiana. She documents her time as a 4-H member during high school and how the extension agents genuinely cared for the club members. She also discusses how a job cleaning houses led her to earn her B.S. degree from Southern University. She discusses her time as a merchandiser for Goudchaux's department store and as an instructor at Alcorn State and Virginia Tech universities. Eventually she earned her Ph.D. from Oklahoma State University and joined the faculty at Southern University. She illustrates the difference between teaching in a college setting and an extension setting. Eubanks describes various aspects of extension, from purchasing her first sewing machine through extension to the new ability of agents to deliver presentations to community members via YouTube."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/historycoopexten/Eubanks_Gina_T4315.abs.pdf	"Gina E. Eubanks was born on June 11, 1956. She is a native of Clinton, East Feliciana Parish, Louisiana. She is the daughter of L.E. Eubanks and Ora (Davis) Eubanks. She participated in 4-H during high school. She attended Southern University and received a B.S. degree in clothing and textiles in 1977. Following her B.S. degree, she attended Oklahoma State University and earned a master?s degree in clothing and textiles in 1978. She also received a PhD in home economics from Oklahoma State University in 1987. In 1990, she joined Southern University as the coordinator of family and consumer sciences. She was named vice chancellor for extension in 2002. In May of 2013, she was named program leader of food and nutrition for the Louisiana State University AgCenter." Louisiana Cooperative Extension Oral History Project	"Denver Loupe oral history interview, 2014"	"Loupe, Denver T., -1927"	2014	"Winnie, Wyatt, -1975"	"Loupe provides a biography of his life, documenting his membership in 4-H and Future Farmers of America during his school years, his service in the U.S. Navy, graduation from Louisiana State University, and his service in the Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service. The primary focus of the interview is Loupe's time in extension services. He discusses his philosophy of education as an agent, field days and other extension demonstrations, livestock shows and contests, and the changing technology in the agricultural industry over time."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/historycoopexten/Loupe_Denver_T4312_T4313.abs.pdf	"Denver Loupe was born in 1927 in Gonzales, Louisiana, to Jack Loupe and Linda Gaudin. He grew up on a farm in the Burnside community of Gonzales. During school he was a member of 4-H and Future Farmers of America. He served as the first president of the Ascension Parish 4-H Executive Committee. He attended Northwestern State University for a year before entering the U.S. Navy. After returning from the navy, Loupe returned to Northwestern State University for two more years before transferring to Louisiana State University. He graduated from LSU with a degree in agriculture before earning a master's degree and doctorate, also from LSU. The doctorate is in botany and plant pathology. After earning his doctorate, he taught high school for three years in Ascension Parish. Later he became an extension agent in St. James Parish. He also served as a sugarcane specialist in St. James Parish from 1954 to 1978. During his time as a sugarcane specialist he served as superintendent of the 4-H Plant Science Contest. Beginning in 1972, Loupe headed the Plant Science Division of the Louisiana Extension Program. In 1978 he was selected as director of Louisiana Cooperative Extension Services. In the same year he established the Louisiana 4-H Foundation. He has served on the National 4-H Council Board of Directors and as secretary-treasurer of the American Society of Sugarcane Technologies. He has authored numerous publications."	"Loupe, Denver T., 1927---Interviews.; Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service.; 4-H Youth Development Program (U.S.); Future Farmers of America.; Agriculture--Study and teaching (Continuing education)--Louisiana.; Agricultural extension work--Louisiana.; County agricultural agents--Louisiana--Saint James Parish.; Livestock--Showing--Louisiana." Louisiana Cooperative Extension Oral History Project	"William Richardson oral history interview, 2014"	"Richardson, William B., -1944"	2014	"Cramer, Jennifer A.,"	"Richardson begins the interview by speaking about his grandparents. He also discusses life in rural Missouri and what it was like to live on a farm in the Kennett area. This includes social outlets such as cruising, going to the movies, basic farm chores, crops, and a typical workday on the farm. He also details his time at Arkansas State University. He discusses mandatory ROTC service, the basketball team, and what college campuses were like during the sixties and the Vietnam War era. Richardson notes the differences between college athletes today and when he was in school, the political awareness of students today versus his time in school, and what it was like to play with the first black basketball player at Arkansas State University. He notes how those experiences helped him to be more diverse as an administrator later in his career. Richardson also discusses how people depended on extension agents for information. County agents helped deliver information to the people in a much different manner than today. Today's agents have more technology and other avenues to disseminate information, though their motivations remain the same."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/historycoopexten/Richardson_William_T4316.abs.pdf	"William Richardson was born in southeast Missouri in 1944 to William Richardson, Sr. and Pauline Gunnin. He was raised on a soybean-cotton farm near Kennett, Missouri. He attended Dearing public schools until he graduated from high school. After high school, he attended Arkansas State University, where he earned a B.S. degree in 1966, and a master's degree in 1968. He received his doctorate degree in agricultural education from the University of Missouri in 1972. From 1972 until 1984, he taught at Purdue University, where he was recognized twice as an Outstanding Teacher, and once as an Outstanding Academic Advisor by the University's Department of Education. He joined the faculty of Louisiana State University as a professor in 1984. He has served in various national and international leadership capacities as well as in numerous administrative capacities and on many boards and committees. He's published numerous articles and textbooks, and has served as the chairperson for various master's theses and doctoral dissertations. He currently serves as Director of Louisiana Cooperative Extension Service and LSU Vice-President for Agriculture and Dean for the College of Agriculture."	"Richardson, William B., 1944---Interviews.; Arkansas State University--Students.; Arkansas State University--Sports.; Farm life--Missouri.; Agricultural extension work--United States.; County agricultural agents--United States.; College students--Political activity--United States.; College athletes--United States.; Discrimination in sports--Arkansas--Jonesboro.; Kennett (Mo.)--Social life and customs--20th century."	1 digital audio file (47 minutes); Index (9 leaves); Abstract (3 leaves)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"William Richardson Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.2387, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." Louisiana Cooperative Extension Oral History Project	"Kenneth Roberts oral history interview, 2014"	"Roberts, Kenneth, -1944"	2014	"Winnie, Wyatt, -1975"	"Roberts discusses his father's career as a meteorologist for the major television networks. He also provides insight into his 4-H club member days and his schooling, particularly his time at the University of New Orleans and his doctoral work at Oregon State University. He primarily focuses on his career with Sea Grant, documenting his time with Clemson University, the National Sea Grant program, and then as a marine economist for Louisiana Sea Grant. Roberts gives insight into the revolutionary nature of his split research and extension appointment, how technology and personal computers impacted extension work, racial tensions with Vietnamese and Cambodian fishermen, and the relationship between the oil industry and Louisiana fisheries. He also describes how the fishing industry is traditionally a male-dominated industry; the prevailing theme of wages among fishermen; and the political impact of federal, state, and local money in extension. Roberts then discusses the need for the quality control of information within the extension model."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/historycoopexten/Roberts_Kenneth_T4314.abs.pdf	"Kenneth Roberts was born on September 19, 1944, in New Orleans, Louisiana. He is the son of well-known meteorologist Nash C. Roberts and Lydia Leblanc. He grew up in Metairie, Louisiana. He attended public schools and participated in the 4-H club in high school. He started his academic career at the University of New Orleans before transferring to Louisiana State University where he earned his bachelor's and master's degrees in agricultural economics. After receiving his master's degree, Roberts moved to Oregon where he attended Oregon State University. His Ph.D. is in natural resource economics. Upon graduation from OSU, Roberts worked as a natural resource economist and program director for the Clemson University Sea Grant program. He then spent a year working for the National Sea Grant office as a program monitor before returning to South Carolina. In 1978, Roberts returned to Louisiana as a Marine Extension resource economist for Louisiana Sea Grant. In 2001, he became the associate vice chancellor and associate director of Extension for the Louisiana State University Ag Center. He retired from the LSU Ag Center in the fall of 2006." Louisiana Sea Grant Coastal Change Oral Histories Project	"Timothy James ""Timmy"" Vincent oral history interview, 2012"	"Vincent, Timothy James, -1952"	2012	"Wilkins, Darcy,"	"Vincent shares memories from his childhood in Erath, Louisiana, and discusses his lifelong interest in the outdoors. Vincent goes into some detail on his Acadian and French ancestry, the history of Acadians in south Louisiana, and Acadian farming techniques. He recalls efforts to phase out, then reinstitute the Cajun French language and describes the languages spoken in his family. Primarily, Vincent focuses on his role as manager of the Paul J. Rainey Wildlife Sanctuary and the changes he's seen to the coastal wetlands of Southeast Louisiana throughout his lifetime. This includes saltwater intrusion, coastal erosion, increased channelization for commercial shipping, changes in the type and number of plant and animal species present, and impacts on the local culture, economy, and population. He touches on the seafood industry, farming, cattle and horse ranching and early cattle drives in Louisiana, hunting and trapping, the introduction of nutria, Louisiana innovations prodded by a lack of resources, the impact of hurricanes on coastal communities, and government regulations on rebuilding in flood areas."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/lasg/Vincent_Timmy_T4162.abs.pdf	"Timmy Vincent was born in Abbeville, Louisiana, in 1952, and grew up in nearby Erath. Vincent is manager for the Paul J. Rainey Wildlife Sanctuary in Vermillion Parish, Louisiana. At the time of this interview, he had worked there for sixteen years and was living at the sanctuary's headquarters.  Vincent's grandparents were of Acadian and French ancestry; they worked as farmers and furniture store owners. His father was an insurance agent and his mother was a home economics teacher. Vincent is a lifelong resident of coastal Louisiana, a former muskrat trapper, and a speaker of English, French and Acadian French." Davis, Jr. oral history interview, 1999"	"Davis, Edward J. 1923 or 4-2012"	1999	"Alberts, John,"	"Davis discusses his service aboard the USS Kalk as a range finder operator and gunner's mate from June 1942 through December 1945. He was awarded the Purple Heart due to an injury he suffered when the Kalk was bombed in 1944.  After the war, Davis settled in Baton Rouge where he attended Louisiana State University, married and had three children.  He died in 2012 at age eighty-eight." Louisianans in the Military Oral History Project	"Joseph Emile Dupont Jr. oral history interview, 2001-2002."	"Dupont, Joseph Emile, 1922-2005"	2001-2002.	"Abraham, Jennifer,"	"Session I concerns Dupont's early life; his inspiration for joining the Marine Corps; boot camp in San Diego; and his passage through Hawaii, Guam, Midway Island, and Manila.  He talks at length about being stationed in Shanghai in 1941.  The interview ends with the Japanese attack on Manila, where he was in a hospital, on December 9, 1941.; Session II deals with the period between December 1941 and May 1942, during which time Dupont served on Corregidor in the Philippines.  He describes details of life there while under siege by the Japanese, the fighting on Bataan and Corregidor, and his eventually being forced to surrender.; In Sessions III & IV, Dupont describes conditions in several prison camps in the Philippines, including Bilibid Prison in Manila, the hospital at Bilibid Prison, and prison camps in Cabanatuan and Palawan Island.  He recounts details of hard labor including building an airfield in the jungle on Palawan Island, lack of food and clothing, poor shelter, diseases, maltreatment by guards, and encounters with wild animals.  He describes the Battle of Manila, his subsequent liberation from Bilibid Prison, readjusting to life after his freedom, and his homecoming to Louisiana.  He also discusses the ""hell ships,"" Japanese ships carrying American prisoners of war that were sunk unknowingly by American submarines, and the massacre of American POWs on Palawan Island on December 14, 1944.; Session V concerns the postwar rehabilitation of Dupont and his close friends, all of whom had war-related disabilities.  He describes his homecoming, meeting and marrying his wife, creating a life as a visually impaired veteran, and his work for the Department of Veterans Affairs.; In Session VI, Dupont tells of his childhood in Plaquemine in the 1920s and 1930s, the Mississippi River flood of 1927, his family background, life along the river, the Depression, his schooling, activities of teenagers, and joining the Marines."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/military/Dupont_Joseph_T2037-2042.abs.pdf	"Joseph Emile Dupont Jr. was born on February 2, 1922, in Plaquemine, La.  He graduated from Plaquemine High School in 1940 and joined the U.S. Marine Corps.  Dupont served in the Pacific Theater during World War II, fighting at the Battle of Corregidor where he was taken prisoner by the Japanese in May 1942.  He was held captive at Cabanatuan, Palawan Island, and Manila in the Philippines until January 1945.  After returning to the United States, he married Angela Hannon on September 5, 1946.  They moved back to Plaquemine and had six children.  Dupont worked in the Iberville Parish Department of Veterans Affairs as a veterans' service officer until retiring in 1980.  He died in 2005." McCaffery during the Vietnam War."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/military/Ammon_Richard_T1661.abs.pdf	"Richard E. Ammon Jr. was born in Richmond, Ind. One of his longest assignments was with the U.S.S. Kidd from 1959 to 1963.  He retired in December 1974 and was residing in Winter Park, Fla., at the time of this interview." LSU History Oral History Project: Alumni	"Albert L. Clary oral history interview, 1993-1994."	"Clary, Albert Lloyd, 1926-1999"	1993-1994.	"Besch, Everett Dickman, -1924"	"Clary discusses his family background and education, early experiences with LSU in the 1930s before attending, veterans, including himself, returning to the university after World War II and university issues specific to them after the war and his involvement in them. Clary also relates his military service during the Korean War.  Additionally, he describes his participation in the changes in the LSU Office of the Registrar, including technology implementation, raising admission standards, and the university's admissions policy on African Americans and the desegregation of LSU.  He also discusses administrative topics such as response to student protests, the growth of both the physical campus and university academic programs, and student discipline.  Clary also remembers various administrators from his tenure at LSU."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_alumni/Clary_Albert_all_tapes.abs.pdf	"Albert L. Clary, Jr. was born in Opelousas, La., on 27 January 1926 and died on 21 April 1999 in Baton Rouge.  He entered LSU as a student in 1942, but his service in the Navy during World War II interrupted his education.  He returned in 1946 and completed a bachelor of arts and master's degree in education.  While teaching in the public school system from 1948 to 1950, Clary obtained a position at LSU as the assistant to the university registrar, but soon thereafter he was called to active service in the army for the Korean War.  His service there included devising and implementing an education program for Chinese and Korean prisoners of war.  In 1952 he returned to LSU as assistant to the registrar and became the coordinator of institutional research.  Four years later he became the registrar of the university.  Upon the dissolution of the registrar's office, Clary became the director of academic services.  In 1986, he became the executive assistant to the vice chancellor for academic affairs.  Clary retired from LSU in 1988.  He was an active member in a number of professional organizations throughout his career including, AACRAO and SACRAO."	"Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.)--Admission.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.)--Students.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.).--Office of the Registrar.; Korean War, 1950-1953--Naval operations, American.; Education, Higher--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; College integration--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; College integration--Law and legislation--Louisiana."	"6 sound cassettes (8 hours, 45 minutes); Transcript (386 p.)"	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Albert L. Hoover oral history interview, 1999"	"Hoover, Jimmie H. 1930-2000"	1999	"Hebert, Mary J.,"	"Hoover describes his early life and education in Arkansas, his service in the U.S. Air Force, life in Libya during the 1950s, his library science training at Louisiana State University, the politics of the LSU-Baton Rouge and LSU-New Orleans library systems during the 1960s, his work with the American Legion, and integration at LSU-Baton Rouge and LSU-New Orleans."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_alumni/Hoover_Jimmie_T1824_T1825.abs.pdf	"Jimmie H. After his stint in the Air Force, Hoover started his master's study in library science at Louisiana State University, finishing his M.S. degree in 1958.  He worked in a succession of positions at the LSU-Baton Rouge and LSU-New Orleans libraries, including heading the Business Administration and Government Documents departments from 1968 until his retirement from LSU in 1984.  After retiring, he worked with the East Baton Rouge Parish Library and at the Centroplex Library.  He was married to Lillian Fitzgerald Hoover for forty years.  He died on April 1, 2000, at age 69." "The interview covers the life, career, political beliefs, and connections of John McKeithen up to 1993.  Significant topics include race relations, development of the Louisiana economic and environmental industry, state and federal politics and political figures, and history and staff of LSU during the years of McKeithen's involvement."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_alumni/McKeithen_John_T473.abs.pdf	"John J. McKeithen was born in Grayson, Caldwell Parish, La., in May 1918.  He graduated from LSU in 1940 and LSU Law School in 1942.  McKeithen married Marjorie Funderburk in 1942 and they had six children, including son Fox, who followed his father into a life of politics.  John McKeithen was elected to the Louisiana House of Representatives and served as floor leader under Gov. Earl Long in 1947.  He was elected governor himself in 1963, running as a segregationist Democrat, and served two consecutive terms in this office until 1972.  McKeithen was appointed to the LSU Board of Supervisors in 1981 by then Gov. Dave Treen.  John J. McKeithen died in June 1999 at the age of 81."
