LSU History Oral History Project: Alumni	"Glenn Lewis McMullen oral history interview, 1996"	"McMullen, Glenn L., "	1996	"Hebert, Mary J.,"	"Glenn McMullen recalls his years at Louisiana State University as an undergraduate and graduate student in the mid to late 1960s and early 1970s. He discusses his anti-Vietnam War activism, especially a 1967 protest that he helped organize with fellow philosophy student, Don Baker. He shares memories of his ROTC duties, his fraternity involvement with Delta Tau Delta, a job at Edwards' Orange Bowl, and of philosophy classes, professors, and fellow students. He recalls people's reactions to the Kennedy and King assassinations. He discusses growing up in Kenner, Louisiana, his early education, high school fraternity culture, and a few memories of race relations and school desegregation."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_alumni/McMullen_Glenn_T1100_T1101.pdf	"Glen Lewis McMullen was born in 1945, in Washington, D.C. His father, Louie McMullen, was a World War II navy veteran who worked for the U.S. Coast and Geodetic Survey in New Orleans. His mother, Jean Cloud, was primarily a homemaker. McMullen grew up in Kenner, Louisiana, and attended East Jefferson High School in Metairie. He began his college career in 1963 at Northeast Louisiana State College, but soon transferred to LSU-New Orleans, and then to LSU-Baton Rouge in 1964. He received several degrees form LSU: a B.A. in Philosophy in 1968, an M.A. in European History in 1972, and an MLIS in 1979. He has worked for the New Orleans Public Library, LSU Libraries, and the Indiana Historical Society. McMullen is now an independent contractor in publishing, living with his wife, Judy, in Austin, Texas." LSU History Oral History Project: Alumni	"Thomas Fuller Ruffin oral history interview, 2000-2005."	"Ruffin, Thomas F. "	2000-2005.	"Abraham, Jennifer,"	"Session I, which is transcribed, describes Ruffin's family and early life in Shreveport and Dallas, an incident where he was severely burned as a child when his nightgown caught on fire, his favorite teachers and subjects in elementary and high school, traveling for school clubs and on a trip through the West with his extended family, his hearing about the bombing of Pearl Harbor and losing friends in World War II, and his attending LSU and the activities he participated in as a student there.; Session II, which is transcribed, describes his youth and experience of the Depression in Shreveport and Dallas, his father's employment with Acme Brick Company, recreation and shopping in Shreveport and Dallas, transportation, his diverse neighborhood and classmates at Alexander School in Shreveport, religious beliefs, downtown Shreveport, Louisiana politicians and governors, C.E. Byrd and Fair Park High Schools in Shreveport, his coursework at LSU and student life there in the early to mid-1940s, ROTC and military service with the Navy, radar school and engineering classes at the University of Illinois and Columbia University, his experiences in Los Angeles and New York while enlisted, the perks of being in uniform during the war, his involvement with the Jaycees, accounts of veterans from the Civil War and World Wars I & II, and the devastation in Europe after World War II.; Session III, which is transcribed, describes classes and experiences at LSU before and after he served in World War II, military training at LSU, campus buildings, dining and recreation around campus, downtown Baton Rouge, urban transportation, the effect of students leaving for the war, dances, his favorite classes and professors, military leaders at LSU, daily life in ROTC, and how ROTC prepared him for the Navy.; Session IV, which is transcribed, relates recollections of Navy service in Los Angeles, Honolulu, Shanghai, and Hong Kong; political strife in China between Nationalists and Communists; people he befriended or helped in Hong Kong and Shanghai, including a man who wrote on scrolls and a little boy who helped him escape a fire fight; prostitution in China; people living on the streets and the high death rate; his view of Chinese culture and customs; his duties on board ship and on shore patrol; the process of being discharged from the Navy; providing medical aid to a boy who later died of cholera; trying to resolve fights among enlisted men and between enlisted men and locals; receiving mail on the ship; and his feelings on veterans of different wars.; Session V, which is transcribed, describes his work for the Acme Brick Company in Fort Worth and Shreveport; his involvement with the Jaycees in Shreveport and the community issues they tackled; marrying his wife, Joyce Toler, and their honeymoon; service as Jaycees state president then national vice president, including campaigning for positions and campaigns he undertook like teen driving safety and anti-fly and mosquito spraying; his meetings with several U.S. presidents; a story about Earl Long; his positive experiences from the Jaycees and feeling that the organization has weakened; and understanding other cultures and getting along with people he meets.; Session VI, which is indexed, discusses his work with Redman Industries in California, Merrill Lynch in San Antonio, and the Frances I. du Pont Company in Shreveport; his experiences in the brokerage business, including changes over time, technology, buyouts from other companies, female and minority employees, and stock strategies; service with the LSU Alumni Association; his perception that Louisiana lags behind; service with other organizations and boards; incidents of racism he's witnessed; information about his family; his interest in history, articles he's written, and the research and publishing of ""Under Stately Oaks; "" and interesting facts from LSU's history."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_alumni/Ruffin_Thomas_all_tapes.abs.pdf	"Thomas Fuller Ruffin was born in Shreveport, La., in 1925, and graduated from C.E. Byrd High School.  He served with the U.S. Navy during World War II in the Atlantic, Caribbean, and Pacific, and continued to serve in China after the war.  Ruffin graduated from Louisiana State University with a B.S. in Mechanical Engineering in 1947.  He was the president of Ruffin Brick Co. and Ruffin Transportation, Inc., then worked for four decades in the stock brokerage industry, retiring as Vice President of Smith Barney, Inc.  Ruffin served on the board of many organizations during his lifetime, including the Volunteers of America, the LSU Athletic Council, and the Louisiana Historical Association.  He also served as National Vice President of the U.S. Jaycees. Ruffin published over 75 articles on the history of the Ark-La-Tex area, and was the author of ""Under Stately Oaks: A Pictorial History of LSU.""  He was married to Joyce Lucille Toler and after her death married Carol Miller Baker.  Ruffin and Baker were married for thirteen years until his death on April 30, 2009."	"Ruffin, Thomas F.--Interviews.; Ruffin, Joyce Lucille Toler.; United States.--Navy--Military life.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College--Students.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College.--Reserve Officers Training Corps.; Acme Brick Company--Employees.; Redman Industries--Employees.; Merrill Lynch & Co. LSU History Oral History Project: Faculty & Adminstrators	"Harold V. Andersen oral history interview, 1999"	"Andersen, Harold Veral, 1907-2000"	1999	"Schiebout, Judith A.; Picou, Edward B.,"	"Anderson discusses his early years in Yuma, Colorado and how fossil hunting with his father, Perry, in northeastern Colorado developed his interest in geology and paleontology.  He discusses how the Andersen paleoindian artifact collection was amassed, why it was important, and how it created associations with museums and curators.  He traces his piecemeal education at the University of Denver, University of Nebraska, LSU, and other institutions and recalls influential professors who shaped his studies and assisted him in finding employment.  He describes fieldwork in Colorado, Nebraska, Alabama, and Louisiana, and other jobs he held including coal miner, carpenter, and archaeological lab supervisor.  Andersen discusses how he came to study and later teach at LSU in the Geology Department and the faculty members in the department in the late 1940s and early 1950s.  He recalls his most significant find: a stunning array of microfossils preserved in mud lump clays collected from the mouth of the Mississippi River with another student, James Morgan.  He talks about exhibits he installed and improvements he spearheaded in the Geology building [now known as the Howe-Russell Geoscience Complex.]  He describes his close friendship with a Romanian professor, Theodor Neagu, and his son, Mike. Andersen touches on many other topics in this dense interview."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_faculty/Andersen_Harold_T1846-1848.abs.pdf	"Harold V. Anderson was born in 1907 outside of Cumberland, Iowa.  His father, Perry, a cattle buyer, and mother, Pauline, moved the family to Yuma, Colorado, around 1910. Andersen started high school in Yuma in 1921 and graduated in 1925.  He attended the University of Denver for one year on a scholarship, but could not afford to continue his studies there. Throughout the 1920s and '30s, Andersen continued his education at various institutions (when funding allowed) and held multiple jobs, working as a carpenter, lab supervisor, and field archaeologist to name a few.  While working in a coal mine in Utah in 1927, he lost half of his thumb in an accident.  He earned a B.A. in Geology from the University of Nebraska in 1940 and soon took a job with the Alabama Geological Survey.  He enlisted in the Army Corps of Engineers during World War II in 1942 and served briefly in Europe.  His engineering unit was sent back to California to train for the invasion of Japan, but the war ended before they were deployed.  He was discharged in 1946 after achieving the rank of captain.  A visit to Louisiana State University that same year led to a graduate assistantship in their burgeoning Geology Department.  His dissertation research, completed in tandem with another student, James Morgan, focused on a foraminiferal assemblage found in mud lump clays from the Mississippi River.  In 1950, four months after receiving his Ph.D., he was recalled to military duty during the Korean War.  He spent the next two years working on a technical manual called ""Geology and Its Military Application.""  After his service, he returned to teaching at LSU and retired in 1977 as Professor Emeritus of the Geology and Geophysics Department. Andersen passed away on June 28, 2000 at age 92."	"Andersen, Harold Veral, 1907-2000--Interviews.; Neagu, Theodor.; Neagu, Mircea.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.).--Department of Geology and Geophysics--Faculty.; Archaeological assemblages--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Archaeology--Fieldwork--Louisiana.; Archaeology--Fieldwork--United States.; Fossils--Colorado.; Fossils--Louisiana--Mississippi River Delta.; Geology--Fieldwork--Louisiana.; Geology--Fieldwork--United States.; Military geology.; Natural history museums--United States.; Paleo-Indians--United States.; Paleontology--Fieldwork--Louisiana.; Paleontology--Fieldwork--United States."	"3 sound cassettes (2 hours, 12 minutes); Transcript (56 leaves)"	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Harold V. LSU History Oral History Project: Faculty & Adminstrators	"Elsie Mae Stallworth Hebert oral history interview, 1993"	"Hebert, Elsie Mae Stallworth, 1925-2012"	1993	"Campbell, Melisse Lynn, -1970"	"Elsie Hebert talks about her choice to attend LSU and study journalism. She discusses the professional fields available for women at that time, dress codes, classes, the Reveille, the journalism school faculty, and her classmates. Hebert describes campus life and calling LSU her home. She discusses her degrees and working for LSU as a professor and adviser to the Reveille. She talks about changes in the journalism school and discusses what LSU meant to her."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_faculty/Hebert_Elsie_T517.abs.pdf	"Elsie Hebert was born in 1925 to Oscar and Iva Mae Boone; she was an only child. She attended Monte Sano Elementary School and Baker High School. Hebert received a bachelor's degree in journalism from Louisiana State University in 1945 and continued her studies there, receiving a master's degree in 1948. After working as a reporter and editor for various newspapers and news programs and teaching for several years at Nicholls State University, she returned to LSU in 1966. She was hired to teach in the English Department and soon became the faculty adviser to the Reveille. She later transitioned into a teaching position with the journalism school where she taught for thirty-five years. She earned a doctorate from the University of Texas at Austin during her first few years as a journalism professor at LSU. She was married to A. Otis Hebert and had two sons. Hebert passed away in 2012." He also describes the LSU campus in the late 1920s."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_faculty/Kniffen_Fred_T77_T78.abs.pdf	"Fred Bowerman Kniffen, professor of geography and anthropology, retired from Louisiana State in 1970, after a career that spanned forty-one years.  Considered a pioneer in the field of cultural geography, he rose to the rank of Boyd professor in 1967.   A prolific writer, Kniffen wrote several articles and books on the cultures of the world and America.  Among his publications are CULTURAL DIFFUSION AND LANDSCAPES (1990), LOUISIANA; ITS LAND AND PEOPLE, THE INDIANS OF LOUISIANA,  LOUISIANA HOUSE TYPES, and CULTURE WORLDS (1951); the latter he co-authored with Richard J. Russell.  Much of his academic work dealt with the role of folklife and material culture in shaping American culture. In 1978 the Association of American Geographers honored him for his role in the development of cultural geography.  Professor Kniffen died May 19, 1993." LSU History Oral History Project: Faculty & Adminstrators	"Miles Edward Richardson oral history interview, 2000-2006."	"Richardson, Miles, 1932-2011."	2000-2006.	"Abraham, Jennifer,"	"Session I, which is transcribed, describes Richardson's early life in Palestine, Tex., between the 1930s and 1950s, including his father's work for the railroad, his mother's domestic duties, life on their farm, animals they kept, their garden, the use of well water and pumps, planting by the moon, folk remedies, the local lumber industry and ""sawmill kids,"" local pageants and events, his mother's death, his crisis of faith, and his first thoughts of becoming an anthropologist.  He also discusses his service in the U.S. Air Force during the Korean War (1950-1954) and his ideas on evolution and anthropology.; Session II, which is indexed, describes his completing a bachelor's degree at Stephen F. Austin State College and starting the master's program at LSU (1957), including duties he had as part of his assistantship, classes and professors, his love of cultural geography, and anthropological theory of cultural evolution.  He gives his recollections of LSU circa 1957-58, especially segregation and mandatory ROTC and civil rights activities.  Richardson describes the doctoral program at Tulane (1958-1965), including work with Dr. Forrest La Violette on political activism of African-American ministers, fellow grad students including his wife Valerie, the popularity of folk music, and the difficulty in finding funding for research.  He also discusses medical and dissertation research in Cali and San Pedro, Colombia in the early 1960s with accounts of life in the local communities and the difficulty of fieldwork.; Session III, which is indexed, gives Richardson's recollections of Cali, Colombia (1962 or 1963), his experiences while teaching at Indiana State College in Pennsylvania, his acknowledgment of the profound influence of Dr. La Violette, prominent theories in anthropology from the 1960s thru 1980s, the role of the Vietnam War and Civil Rights Movement on theories, and a discussion of his anthropological writing, fiction and poetry.; Session IV, which is indexed, discusses Richardson's first years teaching at LSU in the late 1960s, including reactions to the first African-American football players at LSU, campus protests on civil rights, the Vietnam War, the involvement of English Department faculty in the protests, the creation of Free Speech Alley, the reaction to the death of Martin Luther King Jr., Student Government President Ted Schirmer, and the cancellation of the homecoming queen crowning.  He also discusses different reactions to New Archeology by Richardson and William Haag."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_faculty/Richardson_Miles_alltapes.abs.pdf	"Miles Edward Richardson was born in Palestine, Tex., to Mark Carl and Florence Adams Richardson in 1932.  He dropped out of high school in December 1949, a few months before he was due to graduate, and immediately joined the U.S. Air Force.  Richardson stayed in the Air Force for four years, serving in the Korean War while he was stationed in Okinawa, Japan, for two years.  After leaving the service, he slowly began taking college classes and eventually wound up at Stephen F. Austin State College, where he completed his B.S. in biology and history in 1957.  That same year, he started the master's program in anthropology at Louisiana State University.  After only one year there, Richardson transferred to the Ph.D. program at Tulane University.  While a student at Tulane, he married a fellow student, Valerie Woodger.  Richardson was able to go to Colombia on a medical grant and he did his dissertation fieldwork in San Pedro, Colombia, in 1962-63.  For the next two years, while completing his Ph.D. at Tulane in the summers, he taught at Indiana State College (now Indiana University of Pennsylvania).  Richardson earned his Ph.D. from Tulane in the spring of 1965 and started teaching at LSU that fall.  He remained at LSU as a professor of anthropology for the next forty years.  He was Departmental Chair (1970-72) and Acting Chair (1986-87).  He held the Fred B. Kniffen Professorship and the Doris Z. Stone Professorship and served in numerous professional organizations including the Society for Humanistic Anthropology and the Southern Anthropological Society.  Throughout his career, he conducted fieldwork in the southern U.S. and Latin America and authored several books and numerous scholarly articles, as well as several poems and short stories.  Richardson died at the age of 79 on November 14, 2011."	"Richardson, Miles, 1932-2011--Interviews.; Richardson, Valerie Thorn Woodger, 1937-; La Violette, Forrest Emmanuel, 1904-; Haag, William George, 1910-2000.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College--Faculty.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College--Students.; Stephen F. Austin State College--Students.; Tulane University--Students.; United States.--Air Force--History--Korean War, 1950-1953.; Anthropology--Research--Colombia.; Anthropology--Research--Louisiana--New Orleans.; African Americans--Civil rights--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Farm life--Texas--Palestine.; Civil rights movements--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; College students--Political activity--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Vietnam War, 1961-1975--Protest movements--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Palestine (Tex.)--Social life and customs--20th century.; Baton Rouge (La.)--Social life and customs--20th century.; Cali (Colombia)--Description and travel." LSU History Oral History Project: Faculty & Adminstrators	"Virginia Hamilton Vercher oral history interview, 1992-1993."	"Vercher, Virginia Hamilton, 1922-1997"	1992-1993.	"Besch, Everett Dickman, -1924"	"Vercher recalls her experiences working in various administrative secretarial positions and the Personnel Services office at LSU in the 1960s though 1980s. Prompted by Besch, who also often shares his opinions, Vercher offers personal impressions and memories of various administrators, deans, and professors at LSU. She describes the development of the Personnel Services office and her role as the founding employee. She recalls the roles and duties of key campus administrators including Cecil Taylor, Bernard Sliger, Paul Murrill, Lynn Pesson and James Reddoch among others. Vercher goes into detail on university policies and procedures on tenure, academic and non-academic appointments, classified and unclassified positions, job titles, salary levels, personnel forms, biographical data on employees, and many other topics."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_faculty/Vercher_Virginia_T260_T352_T353.pdf	"Virginia Hamilton Vercher was born in York County near Fort Mill, South Carolina, on January 8, 1922. She attended high school and two years of college, then worked for six years at Duke Power Company. She moved to Louisiana with her husband, a Shreveport native who worked for Ethyl Corporation in Baton Rouge. She worked for the Louisiana State Department of Revenue for four years, and after becoming pregnant, spent the next six years as a stay-at-home mom. She started working for Louisiana State University in 1962 as a secretary to Dr. James Upp, Director of Agriculture Experiment Stations, and she continued to work for Upp's successor, Doyle Chambers. She became the secretary to Chancellor Cecil Taylor in 1966, and shortly thereafter, was asked by Bernard Sliger to set up a Personnel Services office at LSU's Baton Rouge campus. Vercher retired as Associate Director of Personnel Services in 1983. She passed away in 1997."	"Vercher, Virginia Hamilton, 1922-1997--Interviews.; Upp, James W.; Sliger, Bernard F.; Taylor, Cecil Grady, 1909-1999.; Pesson, Lynn Louis, 1927-; Efferson, J. Norman--(John Norman), 1912-1990.; Reddoch, James Wilson, 1924-; Louisiana Agricultural Experiment Station.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.).--Office of Human Resource Management.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.).--Office of Academic Affairs.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College--Employees.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.)--Employees.; College administrators--Louisiana--Baton Rouge."	1 sound cassette (1.5 hours); Transcript (92 leaves); Index (31 leaves)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Virginia Hamilton Vercher Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.0182, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." LSU History Oral History Project: Faculty & Adminstrators	"Robert C. West oral history interview, 1992"	"West, Robert C. 1913-2001"	1992	"Anderson, Katharine,"	"Session I, which is indexed, concerns West's education under Carl Sauer at the University of California, Berkeley; his decision to study geography at the University of California, Los Angeles; his work with Clifford Zierer at UCLA; and his interest in the geography of Mexico.; Session II, which is indexed, covers West's work with Carl Sauer, his thesis on Spanish settlement in Mexico near silver mines, his time making maps and surveying European map collections for the Office of Strategic Services during World War II, his study of the Tarascan Indians of Mexico for the Smithsonian Institution, his interest in chinampas farming and related work with Pedro Armillas, and various approaches and theories in the study of geography.; Session III, which is transcribed, describes Carl Sauer and Alfred Kroeber at Berkeley, West's arrival at Louisiana State University, and topics in the study of geography.; Session IV, which is transcribed, concerns West's research on salt marshes in South America, French and Spanish surnames in Louisiana, agriculture in Mexico and South America, and theories on overpopulation in pre-Columbian Mexico.; Session V, which is transcribed, describes West's research on vegetation in the Mexican state of Tabasco, cacao plantations around Comalcalco, colleagues he worked with in Mexico and their research interests, interviewing locals in Mexico on agricultural practices, and his own methods for doing field work.; Session VI, which is indexed, concerns West's methods for doing field work, especially his use of photography, and changes in crops, chinampas farming, and agricultural methods in Mexico.; Session VII, which is indexed, discusses West's work on the geography of the Mexican state of Sonora, faculty members in LSU's Department of Geography and Anthropology, some of West's former students and their research, and a summation of West's research methods."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/distinguished_faculty/West_Robert_alltapes.abs.pdf	"Robert C. West (1913-2001) received bachelor's and master's degrees from the University of California, Los Angeles, finishing in 1938.  He entered the Ph.D. program at the University of California, Berkeley, where he studied under the prominent geographer, Carl Sauer.  West served as a cartographer in the Office of Strategic Services, a forerunner to the Central Intelligence Agency, for four years during World War II.  After the war, he quickly completed his dissertation on colonial mining in Northern Mexico, receiving his Ph.D. in 1946.  West worked as a cultural geographer with the Smithsonian Institution in Mexico City for two years before joining the faculty of the Department of Geography and Anthropology at Louisiana State University in 1948, specifically teaching courses on Central and South America.  He was named a Boyd Professor in 1970 and retired in 1980."	"West, Robert C.--(Robert Cooper), 1913-2001--Interviews.; Sauer, Carl Ortwin, 1889-1975.; Kroeber, A. L.--(Alfred Louis), 1876-1960.; Armillas, Pedro, 1914-1984.; Zierer, Clifford M.; United States.--Office of Strategic Services.; University of California, Berkeley.--Dept. of Geography.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.).--Dept. of Geography and Anthropology.; Geography--Latin America--Field work.; Geography--Research--Latin America.; Geography--Study and teaching--United States.; Agriculture--Research--Latin America.; Agricultural geography--Research--Latin America.; Cacao--Research--Mexico--Comalcalco.; Chinampas--Research--Mexico.; Names, Personal--Research--Louisiana.; Photography in geography.; Plants--Research--Mexico--Tabasco.; Salt marshes--Research--South America.; Tarasco Indians--Research--Mexico." LSU History Oral History Project: Integration at LSU	"Alexander Pierre Tureaud Jr. oral history interview, 1993"	"Tureaud, Alexander Pierre, 1935 or 6-"	1993	"Emanuel-Wallace, Rachel,"	"Tureaud discusses the six weeks he spent as an undergraduate at Louisiana State University in 1953 including his father's legal proceedings to have him admitted, the treatment he faced from students and professors, his disappointment in missing out on a typical college experience, and his loneliness and isolation while at LSU.  He recounts many specific instances of racism, harassment, and discrimination, but also discusses some positive moments."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/integration/Tureaud_A.P._Jr._T375.abs.pdf	"Alexander Pierre Tureaud Jr. is one of six children born to Alexander Pierre Tureaud Sr. and Lucille Dejoie Tureaud.  He attended Joseph S. Clark High School in New Orleans and attempted to enroll at Louisiana State University in 1953, but his application was denied because he was African American.  His father, a prominent civil rights attorney, filed suit against the university to have him admitted.  Tureaud became the first African American to enroll at Louisiana State University as an undergraduate.  He attended LSU for six weeks until the ruling was overturned and he was forced to leave the university.  He finished college at Xavier University and became an educator in New York."	"Tureaud, Alexander Pierre, 1935 or 6---Interviews.; Tureaud, Alexander Pierre, 1899-1972.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College--Students.; African American college students--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; College students--Louisiana--Baton Rouge--Social life and customs.; College integration--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; African Americans--Civil rights--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; African Americans--Segregation--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; African Americans--Louisiana--Baton Rouge--Social conditions--To 1964.; Civil rights movements--Louisiana--Baton Rouge." "Williams discusses his experiences attending Louisiana State University including his time spent studying journalism and working for the Morning Advocate; studying in the English Department; student and fraternity life; military training; the Southern Review and The Reveille; various faculty members; and anecdotes about Cleanth Brooks, Robert Penn Warren, Katherine Anne Porter, and John J. Williams taught English primarily at Yale (1950-58) and the University of Florida (1958-60, 1961-86)." Schorr oral history interview, 2001"	"Schorr, David A., -1944"	2001	"Ramirez, Dominica Dominguez, -1979"	"Schorr discusses his years as an undergraduate at Louisiana State University, his participation in campus activities and fraternity life, and his experiences with the ROTC.  He describes his nearly four years of service with the U.S. Air Force as a radar controller and computer programmer for the SAGE Air Defense System.  His work on SAGE led to employment with IBM and later with the FAA and Lockheed Corporation as a computer programmer."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/ole_war_skule/Schorr_David_T3077.abs.pdf	"David A. Schorr was born in New Orleans on August 4, 1944.  He attended Louisiana State University from 1961 to 1965, where he participated in ROTC and the Arnold Air Society.  He was commissioned in the U.S. Air Force in 1965 and stationed at Truax Field in Madison, Wis., and Luke Air Force Base in Arizona.  Schorr began working for IBM in 1969 as an associated programmer at Kansas City Air Traffic Control Center, assisting in the development of the FAA's Air Control Automation Project.  He left IBM in 1981 to work for Lockheed Corporation at the Johnson Space Center in Houston, Tex.  Schorr was a computer programmer for the FAA in Minneapolis, Minn., between 1982 and 1986.  He was employed at the Houston Air Traffic Control System at the time of the interview." LSU History Oral History Project: Military Tradition at LSU	"Wilbur Joffrion oral history interview, 1995"	"Joffrion, Wilbur, -1924"	1995	"Hebert, Mary J."	"Joffrion discusses his family and early life in Alexandria, La., including the Depression and its effects there; his early interest in the military; and decision to attend LSU and West Point.  In addition to campus and social life at LSU, including hazing, he describes the patriotic feeling of the campus during the early years of World War II.  He recounts his experience and opinion of West Point as a student, his teaching career there, and his later military service in Germany and Korea."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/ole_war_skule/Joffrion_Wilbur_T928.abs.pdf	"Wilbur Joffrion was born on November 8, 1924, in Alexandria, La.  His parents, A. Bush Joffrion and Clara Hope Flower, were also native Louisianians.  He attended Louisiana State University, like many in his family, for three semesters (1942-1943) and studied chemical engineering.  During that time, he served as a ROTC company commander.  Joffrion was also a member of the Delta Kappa Epsilon fraternity.  In 1943, Joffrion entered West Point and was graduated in 1946.  He married Beebe Grace in 1951 and together they had four children.  Joffrion obtained a master's degree in education with a minor in political science from Tulane University in 1953.  He then taught at West Point.  During his eleven years of active duty,  Joffrion was stationed in Germany and Korea.  In 1958, he entered the insurance business and transferred to the U.S. Army Reserve.  As a reservist, he was assigned to Baton Rouge, Little Rock, and New Orleans, and he retired 1981 as a brigadier general."	"United States.--Army--Military life.; United States.--Army.--Reserve Officers' Training Corps.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College--Students.; United States Military Academy--Students.; United States Military Academy--Faculty.; Korean War, 1950-1953--Personal narratives, American.; Alexandria (La.)--History--20th century.; Germany--History--1945-1955."	1 sound cassette (1 hour); Transcript (54 p.) Her father was an attorney and her mother a housewife.  She followed her father to college at Ole Miss, where she majored in home economics and graduated in 1956.  She joined the Phi Mu Sorority and after her graduation served one year as a field secretary for the society.  She went to work in the Dean of Women's Office at Ole Miss, where she remained for 10 years before coming to LSU to serve as the assistant dean of women, working specifically with Panhellenic, sororities, and sorority housing, and other student organizations.  She worked for LSU for 20 years before retiring in August 1987." She transferred to the University of Texas, pledged Kappa Alpha Theta, and graduated in August 1953.  She moved to Baton Rouge in February 1953, and taught as a substitute teacher.  In 1958, Simpson was elected president of the Baton Rouge alumni organization of Kappa Alpha Theta.  She helped establish a Kappa Alpha Theta colony at LSU and assisted in the building of their house.  She also held several other local, regional, and national posts in the sorority." LSU History Oral History Project: SGA Past Presidents	"Horace Wilkinson IV oral history interview, 2000"	"Wilkinson, Horace, 1941-2012?"	2000	"Abraham, Jennifer,"	"Horace Wilkinson IV discusses Wilkinson family history; life on his family's sugar plantations; the lives of African-American plantation workers; downtown Baton Rouge in the late 1950s; working summers at Camp Namequoit on Cape Cod; LSU student life in the early 1960s, especially fraternity and sorority life; his impressions of and relationships with university figures including T. Harry Williams, Troy Middleton, and Kerry Pourciau; his father's political career; and Louisiana politics in the 1950s and 1960s, including the political fortunes of some of his ancestors."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/sga/Wilkinson_Horace_T1853_T1854.abs.pdf	"Horace Wilkinson IV comes from a long line of Louisiana plantation owners.  He attended Port Allen Elementary School, graduated from University High School in Baton Rouge, and attended the University of the South for a year before transferring to Louisiana State University.  His father, Horace Wilkinson III, died suddenly in 1961 and his mother, Elizabeth Ann Scales Wilkinson, later remarried.  Wilkinson was student body president of LSU from April to November 1962, and president of Alpha Tau Omega fraternity.  After graduating from LSU, he worked at Louisiana National Bank for nine years.  He was married but later separated from his wife.  He has a son, Horace Wilkinson V, and a daughter, Virginia Carter Wilkinson." LSU History Oral History Project: SGA Past Presidents	"Lloyd F. Love oral history interview, 1999-2000."	"Love, Lloyd F., 1921-2006"	1999-2000.	"Abraham, Jennifer,"	"Love recalls growing up in Monterey, La., on a 40-acre farm.  He primarily discusses his time at LSU as an undergraduate (1938-1942) and law school student (1946-1948), going into detail about ROTC and cadet life, campus activities, athletics, women on campus, tuition and scholarships, student jobs, his term as LSU Student Body President, his friends and fellow students, and other topics.  He discusses his military and pilot training and WWII service with the U.S. Army Air Corps from 1942 to 1945.  He outlines his involvement with the LSU Alumni Federation, the LSU Foundation, and other university-related endeavors.  He talks about Concordia Parish, La., and his campaign to have a levee built around the parish."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/sga/Love_Lloyd_all_tapes.abs.pdf	"Lloyd F. Love was born in Monterey, La., in 1921 to Sadie White Love and James Hartwell Love.  He had one brother, J.H. Love Jr.  Love was valedictorian of his graduating class at Monterey High School and attended Louisiana State University from 1938 to 1942, earning a bachelor's degree in forestry.  As an ROTC cadet, he was called to active duty in the U.S. Army Air Corps upon graduation.  He earned his wings in August 1943 and flew 73 missions from Sardinia in a B-26 bomber.  He served the remainder of the war flying out of Laughlin Field in Del Rio, Tex.  After the war, Love intended to stay enlisted, but changed his mind after being set up on a blind date with Ann Jackson, whom he soon married.  He started law school at LSU in late 1946 and served as Student Body President in 1946-1947.  He received his LLB and JD degrees in 1948 and began practicing in Ferriday, La., that same year.  Love dedicated much of his life to supporting LSU as member and 1959 president of the LSU Alumni Federation, a charter member of the LSU Foundation, and founder and past president of the Concordia Parish LSU Alumni Association.  He successfully campaigned for construction of a ring levee in Concordia Parish, served as city attorney for the town of Ferriday, was active in the Rotary Club and Boy Scouts of America, and was recognized by the Louisiana Bar Association for his pro bono work.  Love was the recipient of countless honors and awards for his military achievements, his work as a lawyer, his involvement with LSU, and his civic involvement in Concordia Parish and the state of Louisiana.  He passed away in 2006 at age 84 and was survived by his wife and four children."	"Love, Lloyd F., 1921-2006--Interviews.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College--Students.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College.--Law School--Students.; Louisiana State University and Agricultural and Mechanical College.--Reserve Officers Training Corps.; LSU Alumni Federation.; LSU Foundation.; United States.--Army Air Forces--Military life.; College student government--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; College students--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Farm life--Louisiana--Monterey.; Flight training--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Levees--Louisiana--Concordia Parish.; Military cadets--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Women college students--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; World War, 1939-1945--Italy--Sardinia--Aerial operations, American.; Concordia Parish (La.)--Politics and government--20th century.; Louisiana--Politics and government--20th century."	"3 sound cassettes (4 hours, 17 minutes); Transcript (128 leaves)"	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Lloyd F. Love Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.1208, Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La."	Physical rights are retained by the LSU Libraries. LSU History Oral History Project: SGA Past Presidents	"Roger Houston Ogden oral history interview, 1994"	"Ogden, Roger Houston, "	1994	"Dean, Pamela, -1946"	"Ogden provides a detailed biography of his life, from his early years and education in Shreveport and Lafayette, Louisiana, through his time at Louisiana State University, to his successes as a lawyer and later as a real estate developer.  He focuses primarily on his undergraduate years at LSU, discussing his campaigns and tenures as Freshman Class and Student Body President; procedures of Student Government Association and Student Assembly; the end of compulsory ROTC for male students; the political climate on campus in the mid to late 1960s; Vietnam War protests on campus; student leaders; Greek organizations; fraternity houses; fraternity hazing and pledging; dormitories; student activities on and off campus; athletics; university administrators; his favorite professors, and much more. Ogden goes into great detail about his experiences as Senatorial intern to Russell Long in the summer of 1967, and gives his insights into Long's character and motivations.  He recounts his time as a lawyer in New Orleans in the early 1970s, his transition into real estate development, and his first few residential and commercial development projects. Ogden discusses the origin of his collection of southern art and touches on many other topics such as racism, integration and desegregation, civil rights; the oil and gas business in Texas and Louisiana; his parents' backgrounds, LSU's Business School, civic improvement projects in New Orleans, and his continued involvement with LSU through the Alumni Association and as a member of the Board of Supervisors."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/university/sga/Ogden_Roger_AllTapes.pdf	"Roger Ogden was born in 1946 in Denver, Colorado to Roger Hadfield Ogden and Mary Catherine Schneider. His parents moved to Shreveport, Louisiana, just after his birth. Ogden started his elementary education at A.C. Steere School in Shreveport, and continued in Lafayette at Hamilton Laboratory School, part of Southwestern Louisiana Institute. He graduated from Lafayette High School in 1964 and entered LSU that same year, joining Kappa Sigma Fraternity and serving as Freshman Class President.  He served as a Senatorial Intern to Russell Long in the summer of 1967 and was LSU Student Body President from 1967-1968. He graduated from LSU in 1968 with a B.S. in Business. He was awarded the Rotary International Fellowship for Graduate Study at the University of London School of Economics and Political Science, but was unable to pursue the fellowship due to the Selective Service Board denying him permission to travel abroad. He soon went on to Tulane University Law School, graduating in 1971. He worked in corporate litigation for several years with Lemle, Kelleher, Kohlmeyer and Matthews Law Firm in New Orleans. In 1975, with LSU classmate James Maurin, he founded Maurin-Ogden, Inc., a real estate development company. Ogden served on the LSU Board of Supervisors, LSU Alumni Association, LSU Foundation, and was involved with the university in many other ways. He is active in countless civic and professional organizations, and has a large art collection that was the basis for the Ogden Museum of Southern Art in New Orleans. Ogden is divorced from Ann Waits; the couple had one son, Field."	"Ogden, Roger Houston--Interviews.; Long, Russell B.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.)--Students.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.).--Board of Supervisors.; Louisiana State University (Baton Rouge, La.).--College of Business Administration.; LSU Alumni Association.; African Americans--Civil rights--Louisiana.; Art, American--Southern States.; Art--Collectors and collecting--Louisiana.; Civic improvement--Louisiana--New Orleans.; College sports--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; College student government--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Greek letter societies--Louisiana--Baton Rouge.; Lawyers--Louisiana.; Real estate developers--Louisiana.; Real estate development--Louisiana.; Vietnam War, 1961-1975--Protest movements--Louisiana--Baton Rouge." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Baton Rouge Bus Boycott	"Dupuy H. Anderson oral history interview, 1998"	"Anderson, Dupuy H. 1918-1999"	1998	"Wallace, Dawn Deann,"	"Dupuy H. Anderson discusses his childhood in a mixed neighborhood and memories of public school segregation in Baton Rouge; discrimination and segregation in the U.S. Air Force that resulted in his being refused assignments; and his experiences with racism and segregation in social gatherings, trains, hospitals, and schools across the South.  He explains his interest in school desegregation, the motivations and concerns of African Americans for desegregation, and his observations of integration in Atlanta, Mississippi, and California.  Anderson also describes his participation in the Baton Rouge bus boycott of 1953, including the leadership of veterans, peoples' providing free rides for African-American commuters, and the limited success of the effort."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/4_boycott/Anderson_Dupuy_T1513.pdf	"Dupuy H. Anderson graduated from McKinley High School in Baton Rouge, La., in 1935, received a B.S. degree from Southern University in Baton Rouge, and a D.D.S. degree from Meharry Medical College in Nashville, Tenn.  He enlisted in 1941 and served with the U.S. Air Force, rising to the rank of major.  He participated in the 1953 Baton Rouge bus boycott and filed suit to desegregate the undergraduate division of Louisiana State University.  His daughter, Freya Anderson Rivers, was one of six African-American undergraduates to integrate LSU in 1964." At the time of this interview, Batiste was on the janitorial staff at McKinley High School in Baton Rouge where he had worked since 1980." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Baton Rouge Bus Boycott	"Reginald R. Brown, Sr. oral history interview, 1998"	"Brown, Reginald R., -1946"	1998	"Pang, Jeong Suk,"	"Brown shares his memories and information gleaned from his parents' generation about the 1953 Baton Rouge Bus Boycott. He describes various aspects of the boycott including the bus system in Baton Rouge and Scotlandville, segregated seating, carpooling and free rides, meetings, organization, and fundraising. He describes the role of black churches and ministers in publicizing the boycott. Brown also discusses sit-ins and marches during the Civil Rights Movement of the 1960s.  Brown touches on black churches and businesses in the community, politics and law enforcement in Baton Rouge, and describes changes he's seen over time in the black community since desegregation."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/4_boycott/Brown_Reginald_T1503.pdf	"Reginald Brown was born in Baton Rouge, La., in 1946 to Walter and Teresa Bell Brown.  He graduated from Thomas A. Levy High School in 1964 and went on to Southern University.  He worked as an East Baton Rouge Parish sheriff's deputy for twenty-five years and was elected Baton Rouge City Constable in 2000.  Brown has served in organizations such as Holiday Helpers, Inc. of Baton Rouge, Alcohol/Drug Detox Board, the YMCA, and the Louisiana Bar Disciplinary Board.  He is the father of two sons and a daughter." She discusses the role of athletics at McKinley, the quality of the athletic programs, and the rivalry between McKinley and Capitol High School.  She ponders the influence of McKinley on Baton Rouge's history and the school's impact on the political life of African Americans in Baton Rouge."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/1_history/Murray_Daryl_Blacher_T1014.pdf	"Daryl Blacher Murray was born on April 2, 1956, in New Orleans, La., to Beverly and Harold Blacher, Sr.  She is one of five children and grew up across the street from McKinley High School in Baton Rouge, La.  Murray attended McKinley High School from 1970 to 1974.  She served as student body president and class president, was named Most Popular and Miss Track, and was a member of the Honor Society.  After graduating from McKinley, she attended Southern University and graduated with a degree in speech communication.  At the time of the interview, she was employed by the East Baton Rouge Parish Planning Commission.  She went on to work as the associate state director for community outreach for the AARP, and in 2009 became the director of the Bureau of Policy, Planning and Evaluation for the Louisiana Department of Social Services." McKinley High School Oral History Project: History of the School	"Eva R. Legard oral history interview, 1995"	"Legard, Eva R., 1924-2005"	1995	"Posey, Carmen,; Jenkins, Shanta,"	"Legard talks about her years at McKinley High School (1938-1942), and the changes she's seen in schools and education. She discusses her favorite classes and teachers, fellow students, discipline, teachers' involvement in students' lives, and the role of academics and athletics. She briefly touches on the Civil Rights Movement and her election to and service on the East Baton Rouge Parish School Board."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/1_history/Legard_Eva_T908.pdf	"Eva Legard was born in Lafayette, La., in 1924, and moved to Baton Rouge in 1938. A 1942 graduate of McKinley High School, she worked for many years at Southern University, retiring from the registrar's office. She was the first African American female member of the East Baton Rouge Parish School Board. Active in promoting public education, she worked with the Girl Scouts and Boy Scouts, and with her church, St. Francis Xavier. Legard was a longtime member and president of the Board of the Baton Rouge Council on Human Relations. In 1986, she received their Powell-Reznikoff Humanitarian Award. She died in 2005 at age eighty." Perry received degrees in divinity and social work from Howard University and spent most of his career as a minister. He married Clytie Fears of Alexandria, La., and died June 15, 2002." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Old South Baton Rouge Businesses	"Albert Domino oral history interview, 1996"	"Domino, Albert, 1924-2001"	1996	"Henry, Rudolph.; Goods, Michael."	"The interview was conducted as Domino drove around the neighborhood in south Baton Rouge know as ""the Bottoms,"" pointing out locations where important community businesses had been, including barber shops, grocery stores and eateries, churches, shoe shops, and music clubs. Domino discusses racial relationships, the reasons for decline in the businesses, and problems with integration.  His observations show how the institutions of south Baton Rouge affected and influenced the community."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/2_businesses/Domino_Albert_T1030.pdf	"Albert Domino was born in ""the Bottoms,"" a south Baton Rouge, Louisiana neighborhood on 1 December 1924.  Domino grew up with his parents, Benjamin Domino and Geraldine Warren, from Point Coupee Parish, and his five sisters (Madeline, Teresa, Ronnie, Avis, and Agnes) and brother (Alec).  He attended the old McKinley High School on East Blvd. and lived in Baton Rouge until the age of eighteen when he joined the army.  In 1946, he left the army and returned to Baton Rouge, where he found work at the Audubon Post Office on Government St. He worked there until his retirement." She received the latter's Powell-Reznikoff Humanitarian Award in 1986.  She died in Baton Rouge on May 7, 2005." Matthews was married and had three children.  He worked in publicity for Baptist churches for twenty-five years and was a World War II veteran.  Matthews passed away in 2002 at age 95." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Old South Baton Rouge Businesses	"Herman Cooper oral history interview, 1996"	"Cooper, Herman, circa 1928-2011"	1996	"Goods, Michael,; Henry, Rudolph,"	"Cooper primarily discusses African-American owned businesses in South Baton Rouge in the 1940s-1960s, describing in detail the locations of business, churches, funeral homes and well-known landmarks in the neighborhood.  He talks about gravel roads, changing street names, former locations of still-operating business and the demolition of buildings.  He discusses the decline of black-owned businesses in South Baton Rouge and his frustration over black-on-black crime.  He describes segregated medical care at Baton Rouge General Hospital and an ambulance service (operated by his employer, Desselle Funeral Home) that took patients to and from Charity Hospital in New Orleans.  He also discusses funeral homes in Baton Rouge, especially those for African Americans."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/2_businesses/Cooper_Herman_T1026.pdf	"Herman Cooper was born in Baton Rouge, La., to [Frank?] Cooper and Cora Johnson Cooper.  He had an older brother, James, and a younger brother, Leander.  At age sixteen, he took a job at Capital Funeral Home and later briefly worked for People's Funeral Home.  He left in 1948 to work for the newly established Desselle Funeral Home, where he stayed for the remainder of his career.  Cooper passed away in 2011 at age eighty-three." She notes the variation between traditional Catholic Masses and those that are more Afrocentric and discusses how the Church has changed over time to increase female participation and embrace Afrocentric themes. McKinley High School Oral History Project: Old South Baton Rouge Social Organizations	"Charles Aubrey Ricard oral history interview, 2005"	"Ricard, Charles Aubrey, -1930"	2005	"Hendry, Petra Munro, -1958"	"Ricard discusses growing up in South Baton Rouge, describing local businesses, schools, and the physical and demographic makeup of the neighborhood.  He gives specifics on the location of particular homes and businesses in the predominantly African-American neighborhood.  He delves into his family's history of owning property in Downtown Baton Rouge since the 1910s or 1920s."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/5_social/Ricard_Charles_T3446.pdf	"Charles Ricard was born in 1930 in Baton Rouge, La., to Wilbert Ricard and Bessie DeCuir Ricard.  He attended elementary school at St. Francis Xavier and graduated from Southern University Laboratory High School in 1948.  His father, Wilbert, was a contractor and Ricard learned the trade from him.  He went on to work for several building and construction firms in Baton Rouge.  Ricard was widowed and met his second wife, Mary, in 1967.  He has three children." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Old South Baton Rouge Social Organizations	"Emerson Nathaniel Bell oral history interview, 2002"	"Bell, Emerson Nathaniel, 1931-2006"	2002	"Faulkner, Barbara,"	"Bell discusses how his upbringing in South Baton Rouge encouraged him to explore the arts, which came naturally to him.  He recalls the influence of his arts education by family members, friends, and other artists in the community. He describes his early works and traces the influence of various artists who instilled in him the values of simplicity, sincerity and hard work.  He recalls influences and opportunities in New Orleans, Chicago, New York, Detroit, Canada and Japan. He expounds on the spiritual influences on his work and how he still draws inspiration from his early life experiences. Finally, he discusses teaching young artists and urging them to resist material interests and build their confidence."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/5_social/Bell_Emerson_T3175.pdf	"Emerson Bell, known for his sculpture, printmaking and painting, was born in Baton Rouge, La.  Bell attended McKinley High School, the Central Area Vocational School, and he studied at the John Payne National College and Charles Wilson Fine Arts Academy.  He also studied under Alvin Batiste at Southern University.  He served in the army from 1953 to 1955, and was stationed in Japan and South Korea. Bell received grants from the Ford Foundation and the National Endowment for the Arts and was the first artist-in-residence in the Baton Rouge Public School System, where he taught art for many years. Bell passed away in 2006 at age 74." He graduated from McKinley High School (1962) and Southern University (B.A., 1966; J.D., 1973). He co-founded the law firm of Pitcher, Tyson, Avery, and Cunningham and was elected Baton Rouge's first African-American city court judge in 1983. Pitcher also was elected judge of the 19th Judicial District Court (1987) and the First Circuit Court of Appeals (1992). He became a full professor and chancellor of the Southern University Law Center in 2003." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Old South Baton Rouge Social Organizations	"Huel D. Perkins oral history interview, 2006"	"Perkins, Huel D. 1924-2013"	2006	"Hendry, Petra Munro, -1958"	"Perkins discusses his education and goes into some detail on his family history.  He discusses the educational opportunities available to African-American students in the Baton Rouge area in the 1930s and 1940s, including McKinley High and the three elementary schools for African-American children.  He describes activities and sports he took part in in the community and through his church and school.  He discusses some of the prominent leaders in the Baton Rouge African-American community.  Perkins also discusses segregation, racism, African-American fraternities, and civil rights activism."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/5_social/Perkins_Huel_T3516.pdf	"Huel D. Perkins was born in 1924 to John E. Perkins, Sr., and Velma Valeria Davis Perkins in Baton Rouge, La.  He attended Southern University Laboratory School for elementary and high school, graduating in 1940.  He attended Southern University for three years until he enlisted with the U.S. Navy to serve in World War II.  After the war, Perkins completed his bachelor's degree at Southern University and went on to receive a master's and Ph.D. from Northwestern University.  Perkins eventually returned to Baton Rouge and joined the faculty of Southern University where he taught music for twenty-seven years.  In 1978, he accepted a position as assistant vice chancellor of academic affairs at Louisiana State University.  Perkins continued his connection to LSU as executive assistant to Chancellor Bud Davis until 1989, when he also became a professor emeritus of humanities at LSU." He attended Xavier University in New Orleans where he studied under printmaker John Scott. After graduating, he taught art in public schools in New Orleans (Alfred C. Priestly High School) and Baton Rouge (McKinley High School and Southeast Middle School) for many years. He is a successful artist known for his cartoons and caricatures." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Old South Baton Rouge Social Organizations	"Nona Mae Dumouil Gray oral history interview, 2005"	"Gray, Nona Mae Dumouil, 1916-2007"	2005	"Hendry, Petra Munro, -1958"	"Gray discusses growing up in Beauregard Town, a racially-mixed neighborhood, in the 1920s, 30s and 40s. She lists her family members who all lived on the same block that her grandfather, Levanski, had purchased from a French family. She recalls the geography of the neighborhood and surrounding areas: downtown Baton Rouge, the riverfront, Catfish Town, and South Baton Rouge. She talks about stores, restaurants, theaters, churches and businesses in the area. She recounts her time at Reddy Street School and McKinley High, and her experience as one of the first African American graduate students at LSU in the 1950s. She discusses race relations in Beauregard Town and Baton Rouge in the 1920s through 1950s."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/5_social/Gray_Nona_T3439.pdf	"Nona Gray was born in 1916 to Henry Dumouil and Beulah Watson Dumouil. She grew up in Beauregard Town, a neighborhood just south of downtown Baton Rouge. Gray attended Reddy Street School and graduated from McKinley High School in 1932. She received her undergraduate degree from Southern University in 1936, and completed her Master's Degree in Education at Louisiana State University in 1954. At the time she attended LSU, she was one of only four African-Americans in the graduate school. Gray married in 1947 and taught at Perkins Road School, McKinley High and Valley Park School until her retirement in 1977." McKinley High School Oral History Project: Old South Baton Rouge Social Organizations	"Ray Roy oral history interview, 2005"	"Roy, Ray, -1931"	2005	"Hendry, Petra Munro, -1958"	"Ray Roy provides biographical details on his experiences growing up in Baton Rouge and speaks at length about his older brother Alvin. Ray discusses Alvin's purchase of the gym (Alvin Roy's Slenderizing Salon and Turkish Baths), the years that he and Alvin worked in the gym together (mid 1950s through late 70s), the struggles of keeping the business afloat, descriptions of the gym and surrounding neighborhood, the prominent sports figures who trained there, Alvin's work setting up weight training programs for multiple pro football teams, and Alvin's family. There is also a discussion of football teams and rivalries in the Baton Rouge area prior to integration."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/mckinley/5_social/Roy_Ray_T3445.pdf	"Ray Roy was born in 1931, the youngest of seven children. His parents were Joseph Thomas Roy and Lula Marie Major. He attended Saint Anthony grade school and Catholic High School, graduating in 1948. He attended Louisiana State University for two years, then joined the U.S. Navy for four years and served in the Korean War. After he left the service in 1954, he worked with his brother, Alvin, in his gym on Oklahoma Street in Baton Rouge. Alvin was an internationally known weight lifting and strength trainer. Ray Roy married his wife Glenda in 1962." A tobacco enthusiast, Brown became interested in Louisiana perique tobacco and has helped revive this dying crop through promotion and entrepreneurship with perique farmer, Percy Martin." Shadows on the Teche Oral History Project	"Steele Burden oral history interview, 1978"	"Burden, Steele, 1900-1995"	1978	"Cox, Robert Ray."	"Robert Ray Cox conducted this interview and others as part of his thesis research on William Weeks Hall and the gardens of the Shadows-on-the-Teche plantation in New Iberia, Louisiana.  In this interview, Steele Burden describes his relationship with William Weeks Hall, the great-grandson of David Weeks, the builder of the Shadows.  He speaks about Mr. Hall's personality and involvement in preserving the house and gardens. He also recollects the features of the gardens and outdoor spaces, the types of plants used, and the location of certain trees and plants on the grounds."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/robertcox/Burden_Steele_T514.pdf	"Steele Burden worked for the city of Baton Rouge and LSU initially as a gardener and later as a landscape architect.  He played a pivotal role in the founding and development of the LSU Rural Life History Museum at Louisiana State University, Baton Rouge, La., by donating the museum's site, Windrush Plantation, his family's home.  Burden was interviewed here because of his association with William Weeks Hall and his familiarity with the gardens of the Shadows-on-the-Teche in the late 1930s and 40s."  Various Topics Oral History Projects	"Leni Riefenstahl oral history interview, 1979"	"Riefenstahl, Leni, "	1979	"Culbert, David Holbrook.; Lozada, Gisela J.,"	"Riefenstahl discusses producing official documentaries for the Nazi regime during the 1930's; her personal contacts with Adolf Hitler, Rudolf Hess, Albert Speer, Josef Goebbels, and other high-ranking government and party officials; description of circumstances and techniques used in making films, particularly TRIUMPH DES WILLENS, SIEG DES GLAUBENS, and OLYMPIA.  Interview is a translation from German to English of an edited version."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/various/Riefenstahl_Leni_T60-62.abs.pdf	"German film director Leni Riefenstahl was born in 1902 in Berlin.  She achieved fame and notoriety for her propaganda film TRIUMPH OF THE WILL and her two part rendition of the 1936 Olympic Games, OLYMPIA, both made for Adolf Hitler's Third Reich.  One of the most controversial figures in the world of film, she had already made a name for herself in her native Germany and abroad when Adolf Hitler came to power in 1933.  With his friendship and support she became the ""movie-queen"" of Nazi Germany,"" a position she could not live down after the fall of the Third Reich.  After the war, she spent four years in a French detention camp for her part Hitler's regime.  In spite of her energetic attempts to continue as a filmmaker and her protestations that she had done nothing but be an unpolitical artist, she never managed to complete another film."	"Hitler, Adolf, 1889-1945--In motion pictures.; Hitler, Adolf, 1889-1945.; Hess, Rudolf, 1894-1987.; Speer, Albert, 1905-1981.; Goebbels, Joseph, 1897-1945.; Propaganda, German--History--20th century.; Motion picture industry--Government policy--Germany.; Documentary films--Production and direction--Germany.; National socialism in motion pictures.; Nazis.; Germany--Politics and government--1933-1945."	3 sound cassettes (3 hours); Transcript (19 p.)	Louisiana State University Libraries Special Collections (http://www.lib.lsu.edu/special)	"Leni Riefenstahl Oral History Interview, Mss. 4700.0053,Louisiana and Lower Mississippi Valley Collections, LSU Libraries, Baton Rouge, La." West Baton Rouge Parish Oral History Project	"Betty Nelson oral history interview, 1996"	"Nelson, Betty Jackson, "	1996	"Morgan, Brenda,"	"Nelson discusses her family; her grandfather, Sam Caldwell, the overseer at the Cohn family's Carolina Plantation who, with Henry Cohn, established Cohn High School in Port Allen; growing up in Port Allen; attending African-American schools there and in Baton Rouge; her university education in Louisiana and California; and her political involvement in West Baton Rouge Parish."	http://lib.lsu.edu/services/oralhistory/abstracts/wbrremembrance/Nelson_Betty_T1062.abs.pdf	"Betty Nelson was a native of Port Allen, La., and attended Port Allen Colored Elementary School and McKinley High School in Baton Rouge.  As a teenager in the early 1950s, Nelson became active in African-American voter registration in West Baton Rouge Parish.  She attended Leland College, Southern University, Los Angeles City College, and the University of Southern California.  Upon returning to Louisiana, Nelson became active in Port Allen politics where she became one of the first African-American women elected to the West Baton Rouge Parish Police Jury."
